The priest will also sprinkle oil seven times before the LORD and put some on the right ear, thumb, and big toe of the person, along with the remaining oil on their head.

The priest will then offer a sin offering and a burnt offering to make atonement for the person. If the person is poor, they can bring one male lamb, fine flour mixed with oil, and two doves or pigeons. The priest will follow the same procedure to make atonement.

This is the law for anyone with a defiling skin disease who cannot afford the regular offerings.

The LORD also spoke to Moses and Aaron about what to do when they enter the land of Canaan and find a defiling disease in a house. The owner must report it to the priest, who will order the house to be emptied before examining it. If the disease is found in the walls, the house will be closed for seven days. If the disease spreads, the affected stones must be removed and the house scraped and replastered. If the disease reappears, the house must be demolished. If the disease does not spread, the house is clean after being replastered.

To cleanse the house, the priest will use two birds, cedar wood, scarlet yarn, and hyssop, following the same procedure as for a person. This is the law for any defiling disease in a house or clothing.This section outlines the laws regarding various bodily discharges and their associated impurities:

1. If a man has a discharge from his body, he is considered unclean. This includes any flow or stoppage of the discharge.
2. Anything he lies or sits on becomes unclean. Anyone who touches these items must wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening.
3. If someone touches the man with the discharge, they must also wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening.
4. If the man with the discharge spits on someone, that person must wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening.
5. Any saddle the man with the discharge rides on becomes unclean.
6. Anyone who touches anything under the man with the discharge must wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening.
7. If the man with the discharge touches someone without washing his hands, that person must wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening.
8. Any clay pot touched by the man with the discharge must be broken, and any wooden item must be rinsed in water.
9. Once the man with the discharge is cleansed, he must wait seven days, wash his clothes, bathe in running water, and then he will be clean.
10. On the eighth day, he must bring two turtledoves or two young pigeons to the priest at the entrance of the tent of meeting. The priest will offer one as a sin offering and the other as a burnt offering to make atonement for him.

For other discharges:
1. If a man has a seminal emission, he must bathe his entire body in water and remain unclean until evening. Any clothing or leather touched by the emission must be washed and remain unclean until evening.
2. If a man has sexual relations with a woman, both must bathe in water and remain unclean until evening.
3. If a woman has her menstrual period, she is unclean for seven days. Anyone who touches her or anything she lies or sits on must wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening.
4. If a woman has a discharge of blood outside her menstrual period, she is unclean as long as the discharge continues. The same rules apply to anything she lies or sits on.
5. Once she is cleansed, she must wait seven days, and on the eighth day, she must bring two turtledoves or two young pigeons to the priest. The priest will offer one as a sin offering and the other as a burnt offering to make atonement for her.

These laws are meant to separate the children of Israel from their uncleanness to prevent them from defiling the tabernacle.

The LORD also spoke to Moses after the death of Aaron's two sons, instructing him to tell Aaron not to enter the Most Holy Place whenever he chooses, lest he die. Aaron must bring a young bull for a sin offering and a ram for a burnt offering. He must wear holy linen garments and bathe before putting them on. He will take two goats from the community for a sin offering and one ram for a burnt offering. Aaron will cast lots for the two goats, one for the LORD and the other for Azazel. The goat for the LORD will be sacrificed as a sin offering, and the goat for Azazel will be sent into the wilderness to carry away the sins of the people.

Aaron will make atonement for himself and his household with the bull's blood and then for the people with the goat's blood. He will sprinkle the blood on the atonement cover and in front of it. He will also make atonement for the altar by sprinkling it with the blood of the bull and the goat. After making atonement, he will send the live goat into the wilderness, symbolically carrying away the people's sins.

Aaron will then remove his linen garments, bathe, and put on his regular garments. He will offer the burnt offerings for himself and the people, making atonement for them. The fat of the sin offering will be burned on the altar. The person who releases the goat for Azazel must wash his clothes and bathe before returning to the camp. The remains of the sin offerings will be taken outside the camp and burned.The remains of the sin offering, whose blood was used for atonement in the holy place, must be taken outside the camp and burned, including their skins, flesh, and waste. The person who burns them must wash their clothes and bathe in water before returning to the camp.

This is a permanent rule: on the tenth day of the seventh month, you must humble yourselves and do no work, whether native-born or a foreigner living among you. On this day, atonement will be made for you to cleanse you from all your sins before the LORD. It is a Sabbath of solemn rest, and you must humble yourselves. This is a lasting ordinance.

The priest who is anointed and ordained to succeed his father must make atonement, wearing the holy linen garments. He will make atonement for the Most Holy Place, the tent of meeting, the altar, the priests, and all the people of the assembly. This is an everlasting statute to make atonement for the Israelites once a year for all their sins, as the LORD commanded Moses.

In Leviticus Unit XI (17:1-16), the LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell Aaron, his sons, and all the Israelites that anyone who kills an ox, lamb, or goat in or outside the camp without bringing it to the entrance of the tent of meeting as an offering to the LORD will be considered guilty of shedding blood and will be cut off from the people. This is to ensure that the Israelites bring their sacrifices to the LORD at the tent of meeting, where the priest will sprinkle the blood on the altar and burn the fat as a pleasing aroma to the LORD. They must no longer offer sacrifices to goat idols, a practice they have followed. This is a lasting ordinance.

Anyone, whether an Israelite or a foreigner living among them, who offers a burnt offering or sacrifice without bringing it to the tent of meeting will be cut off from the people. Anyone who eats blood will have the LORD's face set against them and will be cut off from the people, for the life of the flesh is in the blood, and it is given on the altar to make atonement for souls. Therefore, no one among the Israelites or foreigners living among them may eat blood.

Anyone who hunts and catches an animal or bird that may be eaten must drain its blood and cover it with dust, for the life of all flesh is in its blood. Anyone who eats an animal that died naturally or was torn by beasts, whether native-born or a foreigner, must wash their clothes, bathe in water, and remain unclean until evening; then they will be clean. If they do not wash their clothes and bathe, they will bear their guilt.

In Leviticus Unit XII (18:1-30), the LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell the Israelites that they must not follow the practices of Egypt, where they lived, or Canaan, where they are going. They must follow the LORD's ordinances and statutes to live by them. The LORD is their God.

None of you shall have sexual relations with a close relative. This includes not uncovering the nakedness of your father, mother, father's wife, sister, son's daughter, daughter's daughter, father's wife's daughter, father's sister, mother's sister, father's brother's wife, daughter-in-law, brother's wife, a woman and her daughter, or a woman and her granddaughter. You must not take a woman as a rival to her sister while the sister is alive. You must not approach a woman to have sexual relations during her menstrual impurity. You must not have sexual relations with your neighbor's wife or offer any of your children to Molech, profaning the name of your God. You must not have sexual relations with a man as with a woman; it is an abomination. You must not have sexual relations with an animal, nor shall a woman present herself to an animal to mate with it; it is perversion.

Do not defile yourselves with any of these practices, for the nations that the LORD is driving out before you have defiled themselves with these things, and the land became defiled. Therefore, the LORD punished its iniquity, and the land vomited out its inhabitants. You must keep the LORD's statutes and ordinances and not commit any of these abominations, whether native-born or a foreigner living among you. If you defile the land, it will vomit you out as it vomited out the nations before you. Anyone who commits any of these abominations will be cut off from their people. Therefore, keep the LORD's charge and do not follow these abominable customs, so you do not defile yourselves. The LORD is your God.

In Leviticus Unit XIII (19:1-37), the LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell the entire assembly of Israel to be holy because the LORD their God is holy. They must not steal, deal falsely, or lie to one another. They must not swear falsely by the LORD's name, profaning it. They must respect their mother and father and keep the LORD's Sabbaths. They must not oppress their neighbor or rob them. The wages of a hired worker must not remain with them overnight. They must not curse the deaf or put a stumbling block before the blind but fear their God. They must not turn to idols or make molten gods. They must judge their neighbor righteously, not showing partiality to the poor or favoritism to the great. They must not go about spreading slander or stand idly by while their neighbor's life is in danger.This is a permanent rule: on the tenth day of the seventh month, you must humble yourselves and do no work, whether native-born or a foreigner living among you. On this day, atonement will be made for you to cleanse you from all your sins before the LORD. It is a Sabbath of solemn rest, and you must humble yourselves. This is a lasting ordinance.

He will make atonement for the Most Holy Place, the tent of meeting, the altar, the priests, and all the people of the assembly. In Leviticus Unit XIII (19:1-37), the LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell the entire assembly of Israel to be holy because the LORD their God is holy. They must not steal, deal falsely, or lie to one another. They must not swear falsely by the LORD's name, profaning it. They must respect their mother and father and keep the LORD's Sabbaths. They must not oppress their neighbor or rob them. The wages of a hired worker must not remain with them overnight. They must not curse the deaf or put a stumbling block before the blind but fear their God. They must not turn to idols or make molten gods. They must judge their neighbor righteously, not showing partiality to the poor or favoritism to the great. They must not go about spreading slander or stand idly by while their neighbor's life is in danger.

Anyone who eats it will bear their guilt because they have profaned the holy thing of the LORD; they will be cut off from their people. When you reap the harvest of your land, do not reap to the very edges of your field or gather the gleanings of your harvest. Do not go over your vineyard a second time or pick up the grapes that have fallen. Leave them for the poor and the foreigner. I am the LORD your God.

Do not hate your brother in your heart. Rebuke your neighbor frankly so you will not share in their guilt. Do not seek revenge or bear a grudge against anyone among your people, but love your neighbor as yourself. I am the LORD.

Keep my decrees. Do not mate different kinds of animals. Do not plant your field with two kinds of seed. Do not wear clothing woven of two kinds of material. If a man has sexual relations with a woman who is a slave promised to another man but who has not been ransomed or given her freedom, there must be due punishment. Yet they are not to be put to death, because she had not been freed. The man must bring a ram to the entrance to the tent of meeting for a guilt offering to the LORD. The priest will make atonement for him with the ram before the LORD for the sin he has committed, and his sin will be forgiven.

When you enter the land and plant any kind of fruit tree, regard its fruit as forbidden. For three years you are to consider it forbidden; it must not be eaten. In the fourth year all its fruit will be holy, an offering of praise to the LORD. But in the fifth year you may eat its fruit. In this way, your harvest will be increased. I am the LORD your God.

Do not eat any meat with the blood still in it. Do not practice divination or seek omens. Do not cut the hair at the sides of your head or clip off the edges of your beard. Do not cut your bodies for the dead or put tattoo marks on yourselves. I am the LORD.

Stand up in the presence of the aged, show respect for the elderly, and revere your God. I am the LORD.

Do not degrade your daughter by making her a prostitute, or the land will turn to prostitution and be filled with wickedness. Observe my Sabbaths and have reverence for my sanctuary. I am the LORD.

Do not mistreat foreigners residing in your land. Treat them as native-born and love them as yourself, for you were foreigners in Egypt. I am the LORD your God.

Do not turn to mediums or seek out spiritists, for you will be defiled by them. I am the LORD your God.

Do not use dishonest standards when measuring length, weight, or quantity. Use honest scales and honest weights, an honest ephah and an honest hin. I am the LORD your God, who brought you out of Egypt. Keep all my decrees and all my laws and follow them. I am the LORD.

In Leviticus Unit XIV (20:1-27), the LORD spoke to Moses, saying: Tell the Israelites: Any Israelite or foreigner residing in Israel who sacrifices any of his children to Molech is to be put to death. The members of the community are to stone him. I myself will set my face against him and will cut him off from his people; for by sacrificing his children to Molech, he has defiled my sanctuary and profaned my holy name. If the members of the community close their eyes when that man sacrifices one of his children to Molech and if they fail to put him to death, I myself will set my face against him and his family and will cut them off from their people, together with all who follow him in prostituting themselves to Molech.

I will set my face against anyone who turns to mediums and spiritists to prostitute themselves by following them, and I will cut them off from their people. Consecrate yourselves and be holy, because I am the LORD your God. Keep my decrees and follow them. I am the LORD, who makes you holy.

Anyone who curses their father or mother is to be put to death. Because they have cursed their father or mother, their blood will be on their own head.

If a man commits adultery with another man's wife—with the wife of his neighbor—both the adulterer and the adulteress are to be put to death. If a man has sexual relations with his father's wife, he has dishonored his father. Both the man and the woman are to be put to death; their blood will be on their own heads. If a man has sexual relations with his daughter-in-law, both of them are to be put to death. What they have done is a perversion; their blood will be on their own heads. If a man has sexual relations with a man as one does with a woman, both of them have done what is detestable. They are to be put to death; their blood will be on their own heads. If a man marries both a woman and her mother, it is wicked. Both he and they must be burned in the fire, so that no wickedness will be among you. If a man has sexual relations with an animal, he is to be put to death, and you must kill the animal. If a woman approaches an animal to have sexual relations with it, kill both the woman and the animal. They are to be put to death; their blood will be on their own heads.

If a man marries his sister, the daughter of either his father or his mother, and they have sexual relations, it is a disgrace. They are to be publicly removed from their people. He has dishonored his sister and will be held responsible. If a man has sexual relations with a woman during her monthly period, he has exposed the source of her flow, and she has also uncovered it. Both of them are to be cut off from their people. Do not have sexual relations with the sister of either your mother or your father, for that would dishonor a close relative; both of you would be held responsible. If a man has sexual relations with his aunt, he has dishonored his uncle. They will be held responsible; they will die childless. If a man marries his brother's wife, it is an act of impurity; he has dishonored his brother. They will be childless.

Keep all my decrees and laws and follow them, so that the land where I am bringing you to live may not vomit you out. You must not live according to the customs of the nations I am going to drive out before you. Because they did all these things, I abhorred them. But I said to you, "You will possess their land; I will give it to you as an inheritance, a land flowing with milk and honey." I am the LORD your God, who has set you apart from the nations.

You must therefore make a distinction between clean and unclean animals and between unclean and clean birds. Do not defile yourselves by any animal or bird or anything that moves along the ground—those that I have set apart as unclean for you. You are to be holy to me because I, the LORD, am holy, and I have set you apart from the nations to be my own.

A man or woman who is a medium or spiritist among you must be put to death. You are to stone them; their blood will be on their own heads.

In Leviticus Unit XV (21:1-24), the LORD said to Moses: Speak to the priests, the sons of Aaron, and say to them: A priest must not make himself ceremonially unclean for any of his people who die, except for a close relative, such as his mother or father, his son or daughter, his brother, or an unmarried sister who is dependent on him since she has no husband. For her, he may make himself unclean. He must not make himself unclean for people related to him by marriage and so defile himself.

Priests must not shave their heads or shave off the edges of their beards or cut their bodies. They must be holy to their God and must not profane the name of their God. Because they present the food offerings to the LORD, the food of their God, they are to be holy.

They must not marry women defiled by prostitution or divorced from their husbands, because priests are holy to their God. Regard them as holy, because they offer up the food of your God. Consider them holy, because I the LORD am holy—I who make you holy.

If a priest's daughter defiles herself by becoming a prostitute, she disgraces her father; she must be burned in the fire.

The high priest, the one among his brothers who has had the anointing oil poured on his head and who has been ordained to wear the priestly garments, must not let his hair become unkempt or tear his clothes. He must not enter a place where there is a dead body. He must not make himself unclean, even for his father or mother, nor leave the sanctuary of his God or desecrate it, because he has been dedicated by the anointing oil of his God. I am the LORD.The anointing of his God is upon him: I am the LORD. 

A priest must marry a virgin from his own people. He should not marry a widow, a divorced woman, a defiled woman, or a prostitute. This ensures that his descendants remain holy, as I am the LORD who sanctifies him.

The LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell Aaron that any of his descendants with a physical defect should not approach to offer the bread of God. This includes anyone who is blind, lame, disfigured, or deformed, or has a broken foot or hand, a hunchback, dwarfism, an eye defect, skin disease, or damaged testicles. Such individuals may eat the holy food but must not approach the veil or the altar to avoid desecrating the holy places, as I am the LORD who sanctifies them.

Moses conveyed these instructions to Aaron, his sons, and all the Israelites.

The LORD spoke to Moses again, instructing him to tell Aaron and his sons to treat the holy offerings of the Israelites with respect and not to profane His holy name. Anyone who approaches the holy offerings while unclean will be cut off from God's presence. This includes those with skin diseases, discharges, or those who have touched anything unclean, such as a dead body or certain insects. They must bathe and wait until evening to be clean and then may eat the holy food.

Priests must not eat animals that died naturally or were killed by other animals, as this would defile them. They must follow these rules to avoid sin and death, as I am the LORD who sanctifies them.

No outsider may eat the holy food, but a priest's purchased servant or those born in his house may. If a priest's daughter marries an outsider, she may not eat the holy food, but if she becomes a widow or is divorced and returns to her father's house without children, she may eat it again.

If someone eats the holy food by mistake, they must repay it with an additional fifth. The holy offerings must not be profaned, as this would bring guilt upon the people. I am the LORD who sanctifies them.

The LORD instructed Moses to tell Aaron, his sons, and all the Israelites that any offering brought to the LORD must be without defect to be accepted. This includes offerings for vows or freewill offerings. Animals with defects such as blindness, broken bones, or skin diseases are not acceptable. However, a bull or lamb with a minor defect may be offered as a freewill offering but not for a vow.

Offerings must not come from foreigners, as their animals may have defects. The LORD also instructed that newborn animals must stay with their mother for seven days and can be offered from the eighth day onward. Animals and their young must not be killed on the same day.

Thanksgiving sacrifices must be eaten on the same day and not left until morning. The LORD's commandments must be followed to avoid profaning His holy name, as He is the LORD who sanctifies and brought the Israelites out of Egypt to be their God.Do not harvest the edges of your field or gather the leftovers from your harvest. Leave them for the poor and the foreigner. I am the LORD your God.

The LORD spoke to Moses, saying: "Tell the Israelites that on the first day of the seventh month, you are to have a day of rest, a sacred assembly commemorated with trumpet blasts. Do no regular work and present a food offering to the LORD."

The LORD spoke to Moses again, saying: "On the fifteenth day of the seventh month, the LORD's Festival of Tabernacles begins, and it lasts for seven days. The first day is a sacred assembly; do no regular work. For seven days, present food offerings to the LORD, and on the eighth day hold a sacred assembly and present a food offering to the LORD. It is the closing special assembly; do no regular work."

These are the LORD's appointed festivals, which you are to proclaim as sacred assemblies for bringing food offerings to the LORD—burnt offerings and grain offerings, sacrifices and drink offerings required for each day. These offerings are in addition to those for the LORD's Sabbaths and in addition to your gifts and whatever you have vowed and all the freewill offerings you give to the LORD.

The LORD spoke to Moses, saying: "On the tenth day of the seventh month is the Day of Atonement. Hold a sacred assembly and deny yourselves, and present a food offering to the LORD. Do no work on that day because it is the Day of Atonement, when atonement is made for you before the LORD your God. Anyone who does not deny themselves on that day must be cut off from their people. I will destroy anyone among you who does any work on that day. You shall do no work at all. This is to be a lasting ordinance for the generations to come, wherever you live. It is a day of sabbath rest for you, and you must deny yourselves. From the evening of the ninth day of the month until the following evening, you are to observe your sabbath."

The LORD spoke to Moses, saying: "On the fifteenth day of the seventh month, after you have gathered the crops of the land, celebrate the festival to the LORD for seven days; the first day is a day of rest, and the eighth day also is a day of rest. On the first day, you are to take branches from luxuriant trees—from palms, willows, and other leafy trees—and rejoice before the LORD your God for seven days. Celebrate this as a festival to the LORD for seven days each year. This is to be a lasting ordinance for the generations to come; celebrate it in the seventh month. Live in temporary shelters for seven days: All native-born Israelites are to live in such shelters so your descendants will know that I had the Israelites live in temporary shelters when I brought them out of Egypt. I am the LORD your God."

So Moses announced to the Israelites the appointed festivals of the LORD.

The LORD spoke to Moses, saying: "Command the Israelites to bring you clear oil of pressed olives for the light so that the lamps may be kept burning continually. Outside the curtain that shields the ark of the covenant law in the tent of meeting, Aaron is to tend the lamps before the LORD from evening till morning, continually. This is to be a lasting ordinance for the generations to come. The lamps on the pure gold lampstand before the LORD must be tended continually.

Take the finest flour and bake twelve loaves of bread, using two-tenths of an ephah for each loaf. Arrange them in two stacks, six in each stack, on the table of pure gold before the LORD. By each stack, put some pure incense as a memorial portion to represent the bread and to be a food offering presented to the LORD. This bread is to be set out before the LORD regularly, Sabbath after Sabbath, on behalf of the Israelites, as a lasting covenant. It belongs to Aaron and his sons, who are to eat it in the sanctuary area because it is a most holy part of their perpetual share of the food offerings presented to the LORD."

Now the son of an Israelite mother and an Egyptian father went out among the Israelites, and a fight broke out in the camp between him and an Israelite. The son of the Israelite woman blasphemed the Name with a curse; so they brought him to Moses. (His mother's name was Shelomith, the daughter of Dibri the Danite.) They put him in custody until the will of the LORD should be made clear to them.

Then the LORD said to Moses: "Take the blasphemer outside the camp. All those who heard him are to lay their hands on his head, and the entire assembly is to stone him. Say to the Israelites: 'Anyone who curses their God will be held responsible; anyone who blasphemes the name of the LORD is to be put to death. The entire assembly must stone them. Whether foreigner or native-born, when they blaspheme the Name, they are to be put to death.

Anyone who takes the life of a human being is to be put to death. Anyone who takes the life of someone's animal must make restitution—life for life. Anyone who injures their neighbor is to be injured in the same manner: fracture for fracture, eye for eye, tooth for tooth. The one who has inflicted the injury must suffer the same injury. Whoever kills an animal must make restitution, but whoever kills a human being is to be put to death. You are to have the same law for the foreigner and the native-born. I am the LORD your God.'"

Then Moses spoke to the Israelites, and they took the blasphemer outside the camp and stoned him. The Israelites did as the LORD commanded Moses.

The LORD spoke to Moses at Mount Sinai, saying: "Speak to the Israelites and say to them: 'When you enter the land I am going to give you, the land itself must observe a sabbath to the LORD. For six years sow your fields, and for six years prune your vineyards and gather their crops. But in the seventh year, the land is to have a year of sabbath rest, a sabbath to the LORD. Do not sow your fields or prune your vineyards. Do not reap what grows of itself or harvest the grapes of your untended vines. The land is to have a year of rest. Whatever the land yields during the sabbath year will be food for you—for yourself, your male and female servants, the hired worker and temporary resident who live among you, as well as for your livestock and the wild animals in your land. Whatever the land produces may be eaten.

Count off seven sabbath years—seven times seven years—so that the seven sabbath years amount to a period of forty-nine years. Then have the trumpet sounded everywhere on the tenth day of the seventh month; on the Day of Atonement sound the trumpet throughout your land. Consecrate the fiftieth year and proclaim liberty throughout the land to all its inhabitants. It shall be a jubilee for you; each of you is to return to your family property and to your own clan. The fiftieth year shall be a jubilee for you; do not sow and do not reap what grows of itself or harvest the untended vines. For it is a jubilee and is to be holy for you; eat only what is taken directly from the fields.

In this Year of Jubilee everyone is to return to their own property. If you sell land to any of your own people or buy land from them, do not take advantage of each other. You are to buy from your own people on the basis of the number of years since the Jubilee. And they are to sell to you on the basis of the number of years left for harvesting crops. When the years are many, you are to increase the price, and when the years are few, you are to decrease the price, because what is really being sold to you is the number of crops. Do not take advantage of each other, but fear your God. I am the LORD your God.

Follow my decrees and be careful to obey my laws, and you will live safely in the land. Then the land will yield its fruit, and you will eat your fill and live there in safety. You may ask, "What will we eat in the seventh year if we do not plant or harvest our crops?" I will send you such a blessing in the sixth year that the land will yield enough for three years. While you plant during the eighth year, you will eat from the old crop and will continue to eat from it until the harvest of the ninth year comes in.

The land must not be sold permanently because the land is mine and you reside in my land as foreigners and strangers. Throughout the land that you hold as a possession, you must provide for the redemption of the land.

If one of your fellow Israelites becomes poor and sells some of their property, their nearest relative is to come and redeem what they have sold.If a man has no one to redeem his property and later becomes wealthy enough to buy it back, he should calculate the years since it was sold and repay the excess to the buyer, then reclaim his property. If he cannot afford to buy it back, the property remains with the buyer until the Year of Jubilee, when it will be returned to him.

If someone sells a house in a walled city, they have a year to redeem it. If not redeemed within that year, the house permanently belongs to the buyer and does not return in the Jubilee. However, houses in villages without walls are treated like fields and can be redeemed and returned in the Jubilee.

The Levites always have the right to redeem their houses in their cities. If a Levite sells a house, it will be returned in the Jubilee because their houses are their permanent possession among the Israelites. The fields around their cities cannot be sold as they are their permanent possession.

If an Israelite becomes poor and cannot support themselves, help them as you would a foreigner or temporary resident, so they can continue to live among you. Do not charge them interest or profit from their food. Remember, I am the LORD your God who brought you out of Egypt to give you the land of Canaan and to be your God.

If an Israelite becomes poor and sells themselves to you, do not treat them as slaves. They should be treated as hired workers or temporary residents and serve you until the Year of Jubilee. Then they and their children are to be released and return to their own family and property. They are my servants, whom I brought out of Egypt, and must not be sold as slaves. Do not rule over them harshly, but fear your God.

You may buy male and female slaves from the surrounding nations. You can also buy slaves from the foreigners living among you and their families born in your land. They will become your property and can be inherited by your children as permanent possessions. However, do not rule over your fellow Israelites harshly.

If a foreigner living among you becomes wealthy and an Israelite becomes poor and sells themselves to the foreigner or a member of their family, they retain the right to be redeemed. A relative may redeem them, or if they prosper, they may redeem themselves. The price of their redemption is based on the number of years until the Jubilee, calculated as if they were a hired worker. If many years remain, they must repay a larger amount; if few years remain, they repay a smaller amount. They are to be treated as hired workers and not ruled over harshly. If not redeemed, they and their children are to be released in the Year of Jubilee. The Israelites are my servants, whom I brought out of Egypt. I am the LORD your God.

Do not make idols or set up images or sacred stones to bow down to, for I am the LORD your God. Observe my Sabbaths and have reverence for my sanctuary. If you follow my decrees and obey my commands, I will send rain in its season, and the land will yield its crops and the trees their fruit. Your threshing will continue until grape harvest, and the grape harvest will continue until planting, and you will eat all the food you want and live in safety in your land.

If you do not listen to me and carry out all these commands, if you reject my decrees and abhor my laws, breaking my covenant, I will bring upon you sudden terror, wasting diseases, and fever that will destroy your sight and drain your life. You will plant seed in vain because your enemies will eat it. I will set my face against you so that you will be defeated by your enemies; those who hate you will rule over you, and you will flee even when no one is pursuing you.

If after all this you do not listen to me, I will punish you for your sins seven times over. I will break your stubborn pride and make the sky above you like iron and the ground beneath you like bronze. Your strength will be spent in vain because your soil will not yield its crops, nor will the trees of your land yield their fruit.

If you remain hostile toward me and refuse to listen, I will multiply your afflictions seven times over, as your sins deserve. I will send wild animals against you, and they will rob you of your children, destroy your cattle, and make you so few in number that your roads will be deserted.

If in spite of these things you do not accept my correction but continue to be hostile toward me, I will be hostile toward you and will afflict you for your sins seven times over. I will bring the sword upon you to avenge the breaking of the covenant. When you withdraw into your cities, I will send a plague among you, and you will be given into enemy hands. When I cut off your supply of bread, ten women will bake your bread in one oven and dole out the bread by weight. You will eat, but you will not be satisfied.

If in spite of this you still do not listen to me but continue to be hostile toward me, then in my anger I will be hostile toward you, and I myself will punish you for your sins seven times over. You will eat the flesh of your sons and the flesh of your daughters. I will destroy your high places, cut down your incense altars, and pile your dead bodies on the lifeless forms of your idols, and I will abhor you. I will turn your cities into ruins and lay waste your sanctuaries, and I will take no delight in the pleasing aroma of your offerings. I will lay waste the land so that your enemies who live there will be appalled. I will scatter you among the nations and will draw out my sword and pursue you. Your land will be laid waste, and your cities will lie in ruins. Then the land will enjoy its sabbath years all the time that it lies desolate and you are in the country of your enemies; the land will rest and enjoy its sabbaths. All the time that it lies desolate, the land will have the rest it did not have during the sabbaths you lived in it.

As for those of you who are left, I will make their hearts so fearful in the lands of their enemies that the sound of a windblown leaf will put them to flight. They will run as though fleeing from the sword, and they will fall even though no one is pursuing them. They will stumble over one another as though fleeing from the sword, even though no one is pursuing them. So you will not be able to stand before your enemies.If you continue to disobey me, you will perish among the nations, and your enemies' land will consume you. Those who survive will waste away because of their sins and the sins of their ancestors. But if they confess their sins and the sins of their ancestors, acknowledging their betrayal and opposition to me, I will also oppose them and bring them into their enemies' land. If their stubborn hearts are humbled and they accept their punishment, I will remember my covenant with Jacob, Isaac, and Abraham, and I will remember the land. The land will be deserted and enjoy its sabbaths while it lies desolate without them, and they will pay for their sins because they rejected my laws and despised my decrees.

Despite all this, when they are in their enemies' land, I will not reject or despise them to the point of destroying them completely and breaking my covenant with them, for I am the LORD their God. For their sake, I will remember the covenant with their ancestors, whom I brought out of Egypt in the sight of the nations to be their God. I am the LORD.

These are the decrees, laws, and regulations that the LORD established between himself and the Israelites through Moses on Mount Sinai.

The LORD said to Moses, "Speak to the Israelites and tell them: When someone makes a special vow to dedicate persons to the LORD by giving equivalent values, set the value of a male between the ages of twenty and sixty at fifty shekels of silver, according to the sanctuary shekel. For a female, set the value at thirty shekels. For a person between the ages of five and twenty, set the value at twenty shekels for a male and ten shekels for a female. For a person between one month and five years, set the value at five shekels of silver for a male and three shekels of silver for a female. For a person sixty years old or more, set the value at fifteen shekels for a male and ten shekels for a female. If anyone making the vow is too poor to pay the specified amount, they are to present the person to the priest, who will set the value according to what the person making the vow can afford.

If what they vowed is an animal that is acceptable as an offering to the LORD, such an animal given to the LORD becomes holy. They must not exchange it or substitute a good one for a bad one or a bad one for a good one; if they should substitute one animal for another, both it and the substitute become holy. If what they vowed is a ceremonially unclean animal—one that is not acceptable as an offering to the LORD—the animal must be presented to the priest, who will judge its quality as good or bad. Whatever value the priest then sets, that is what it will be. If the owner wishes to redeem the animal, a fifth must be added to its value.

If anyone dedicates their house as something holy to the LORD, the priest will judge its quality as good or bad. Whatever value the priest then sets, so it will remain. If the one who dedicates their house wishes to redeem it, they must add a fifth to its value, and the house will again become theirs.

If anyone dedicates to the LORD part of their family land, its value is to be set according to the amount of seed required for it—fifty shekels of silver to a homer of barley seed. If they dedicate a field during the Year of Jubilee, the value that has been set remains. But if they dedicate a field after the Jubilee, the priest will determine the value according to the number of years that remain until the next Year of Jubilee, and its set value will be reduced. If the one who dedicates the field wishes to redeem it, they must add a fifth to its value, and the field will again become theirs. If, however, they do not redeem the field, or if they have sold it to someone else, it can never be redeemed. When the field is released in the Jubilee, it will become holy, like a field devoted to the LORD; it will become priestly property.

No one may dedicate the firstborn of an animal, since the firstborn already belongs to the LORD; whether an ox or a sheep, it is the LORD's. If it is one of the unclean animals, they may buy it back at its set value, adding a fifth of the value to it. If they do not redeem it, it is to be sold at its set value.

Every tithe of the land, whether grain from the soil or fruit from the trees, belongs to the LORD; it is holy to the LORD. Whoever would redeem any of their tithe must add a fifth of the value to it. Every tithe of the herd and flock—every tenth animal that passes under the shepherd's rod—will be holy to the LORD. No one may pick out the good from the bad or make any substitution. If anyone does make a substitution, both the animal and its substitute become holy and cannot be redeemed."

These are the commands the LORD gave Moses at Mount Sinai for the Israelites.Chapter and Verse B 1:20 - The descendants of Reuben, Israel's firstborn, were counted by their families and households. B 2:1 - The LORD spoke to Moses and Aaron, saying: 2:2 "The Israelites are to camp by their divisions, each man under his standard with the banners of his family. They are to camp around the tent of meeting but at some distance.

2:3 - On the east side, toward the sunrise, the divisions of the camp of Judah are to encamp under their standard. The leader of the people of Judah is Nahshon son of Amminadab. 2:4 His division numbers 74,600.

2:5 - The tribe of Issachar will camp next to them. The leader of the people of Issachar is Nethanel son of Zuar. 2:6 His division numbers 54,400.

2:7 - The tribe of Zebulun will be next. The leader of the people of Zebulun is Eliab son of Helon. 2:8 His division numbers 57,400.

2:9 - All the men assigned to the camp of Judah, according to their divisions, number 186,400. They will set out first.

2:10 - On the south side will be the divisions of the camp of Reuben under their standard. The leader of the people of Reuben is Elizur son of Shedeur. 2:11 His division numbers 46,500.

2:12 - The tribe of Simeon will camp next to them. The leader of the people of Simeon is Shelumiel son of Zurishaddai. 2:13 His division numbers 59,300.

2:14 - The tribe of Gad will be next. The leader of the people of Gad is Eliasaph son of Deuel. 2:15 His division numbers 45,650.

2:16 - All the men assigned to the camp of Reuben, according to their divisions, number 151,450. They will set out second.

2:17 - Then the tent of meeting and the camp of the Levites will set out in the middle of the camps. They will set out in the same order as they encamp, each in their own place under their standard.

2:18 - On the west side will be the divisions of the camp of Ephraim under their standard. The leader of the people of Ephraim is Elishama son of Ammihud. 2:19 His division numbers 40,500.

2:20 - The tribe of Manasseh will be next to them. The leader of the people of Manasseh is Gamaliel son of Pedahzur. 2:21 His division numbers 32,200.

2:22 - The tribe of Benjamin will be next. The leader of the people of Benjamin is Abidan son of Gideoni. 2:23 His division numbers 35,400.

2:24 - All the men assigned to the camp of Ephraim, according to their divisions, number 108,100. They will set out third.

2:27 - The tribe of Asher will camp next to them. The leader of the people of Asher is Pagiel son of Ochran. 2:28 His division numbers 41,500.

2:29 - The tribe of Naphtali will be next. The leader of the people of Naphtali is Ahira son of Enan. 2:30 His division numbers 53,400.

NUMBERS UNIT I (1:1 - 4:49)

A 3:1 - These are the generations of Aaron and Moses at the time the LORD spoke to Moses on Mount Sinai.

3:2 - These are the names of the sons of Aaron: Nadab the firstborn, Abihu, Eleazar, and Ithamar.

3:3 - These are the names of the sons of Aaron, the anointed priests, who were ordained to serve as priests.

3:4 - Nadab and Abihu, however, died before the LORD when they made an unauthorized offering before Him in the Desert of Sinai. They had no sons, so Eleazar and Ithamar served as priests during the lifetime of their father Aaron.

A 3:14 - The LORD said to Moses in the Desert of Sinai, 3:15 "Count the Levites by their families and clans. Count every male a month old or more." 3:16 So Moses counted them, as he was commanded by the word of the LORD.The LORD commanded Moses to count the Levites by their families and clans. These are the sons of Levi: Gershon, Kohath, and Merari. The sons of Gershon were Libni and Shimei. The sons of Kohath were Amram, Izhar, Hebron, and Uzziel. The sons of Merari were Mahli and Mushi. These are the families of the Levites.

The LORD told Moses to bring the tribe of Levi to assist Aaron the priest. They were to take care of the tabernacle and its furnishings, and serve the community. The Levites were given to Aaron and his sons to help with their priestly duties. Any unauthorized person who approached the sanctuary would be put to death.

The families of Gershon, including the Libnites and Shimeites, numbered 7,500 males from a month old and up. They camped west of the tabernacle, with Eliasaph son of Lael as their leader. Their duties included caring for the tabernacle's coverings, curtains, and cords.

The families of Kohath, including the Amramites, Izharites, Hebronites, and Uzzielites, numbered 8,600 males from a month old and up. They camped south of the tabernacle, with Elizaphan son of Uzziel as their leader. Their duties included caring for the ark, table, lampstand, altars, and other sacred items. Eleazar, son of Aaron, oversaw them.

The families of Merari, including the Mahlites and Mushites, numbered 6,200 males from a month old and up. They camped north of the tabernacle, with Zuriel son of Abihail as their leader. Their duties included caring for the tabernacle's frames, bars, pillars, and bases.

Moses, Aaron, and his sons camped east of the tabernacle, guarding the sanctuary. Any unauthorized person who approached would be put to death. The total number of Levites counted was 22,000 males from a month old and up.

The LORD told Moses to count all the firstborn males of Israel from a month old and up. The total number was 22,273. The LORD took the Levites in place of the firstborn of Israel and their cattle in place of the firstborn cattle. Moses collected five shekels for each of the 273 firstborn Israelites who exceeded the number of Levites and gave the money to Aaron and his sons as commanded by the LORD.

The LORD instructed Moses and Aaron to count the Kohathites from thirty to fifty years old, those who would serve in the tent of meeting. Their duties included caring for the most holy items. Aaron and his sons were to cover these items before the Kohathites transported them, ensuring they did not touch or see the holy things, lest they die. The total number of Kohathites counted for service was 2,750.The families of the Kohathites who served in the tent of meeting were counted by Moses and Aaron as commanded by the LORD. The LORD then instructed Moses to count the sons of Gershon by their families, from thirty to fifty years old, those who would serve in the tent of meeting. The Gershonites were responsible for carrying the curtains of the tabernacle, the tent of meeting, its covering, the sealskin covering, the screen for the door, the hangings of the court, the screen for the gate, and all related cords and instruments. Their service was directed by Aaron and his sons, and they were under the supervision of Ithamar, son of Aaron. The total number of Gershonites counted for service was 2,630.

Next, the LORD instructed Moses to count the sons of Merari by their families, from thirty to fifty years old, those who would serve in the tent of meeting. The Merarites were responsible for the boards, bars, pillars, sockets, and all related items of the tabernacle. Their service was also under the supervision of Ithamar, son of Aaron. The total number of Merarites counted for service was 3,200.

In total, Moses, Aaron, and the leaders of Israel counted 8,580 Levites from thirty to fifty years old, who were assigned to their specific duties and burdens in the tent of meeting as commanded by the LORD.

The LORD then instructed Moses to command the Israelites to remove from the camp anyone with a skin disease, a discharge, or who was unclean due to contact with the dead, to prevent defiling the camp where the LORD dwells. The Israelites obeyed and removed the unclean individuals from the camp.

The LORD also instructed Moses to tell the Israelites that if a man or woman commits a sin against another person, they must confess their sin, make full restitution, and add a fifth of the value to it. If the wronged person has no relative to receive the restitution, it should be given to the LORD for the priest, along with a ram for atonement.

Additionally, the LORD provided instructions for dealing with a wife suspected of unfaithfulness. The husband would bring his wife to the priest with an offering. The priest would prepare a mixture of holy water and tabernacle dust, and the woman would drink it after taking an oath. If she was guilty, the water would cause her belly to swell and her thigh to waste away, making her a curse among her people. If she was innocent, she would be unharmed and able to conceive children.

Finally, the LORD spoke to Moses about the Nazirite vow. A man or woman who takes this vow must abstain from wine, strong drink, vinegar, grape products, and must not cut their hair for the duration of the vow. They must also avoid contact with dead bodies to remain consecrated to the LORD.A Nazirite must not defile himself by coming near a dead body, even if it is his father, mother, brother, or sister. His dedication to God is symbolized by his uncut hair. If someone dies suddenly beside him, he must shave his head on the seventh day of his cleansing. On the eighth day, he must bring two turtledoves or two young pigeons to the priest at the entrance of the tent of meeting. The priest will offer one as a sin offering and the other as a burnt offering to atone for the defilement. The Nazirite will then rededicate his head and bring a year-old male lamb as a guilt offering. The previous days of his vow are void because his consecration was defiled.

When a Nazirite completes his vow, he must bring his offerings to the entrance of the tent of meeting: a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering, a year-old female lamb for a sin offering, a ram for a peace offering, a basket of unleavened bread, cakes mixed with oil, unleavened wafers spread with oil, and their grain and drink offerings. The priest will present these offerings to the LORD. The Nazirite will then shave his consecrated head at the entrance of the tent of meeting and place the hair on the fire under the peace offering. The priest will take the boiled shoulder of the ram, one unleavened cake, and one unleavened wafer, and place them in the Nazirite's hands after he has shaved his head. The priest will then wave them as a wave offering before the LORD. This is holy for the priest, along with the breast of the wave offering and the thigh of the heave offering. After this, the Nazirite may drink wine. This is the law of the Nazirite who makes a vow and brings his offerings to the LORD.

The LORD spoke to Moses, instructing him to tell Aaron and his sons to bless the Israelites with these words: "The LORD bless you and keep you; the LORD make His face shine upon you and be gracious to you; the LORD lift up His countenance upon you and give you peace." By doing this, they will put God's name on the Israelites, and He will bless them.

On the day Moses finished setting up the tabernacle, he anointed and consecrated it and all its furnishings, including the altar and its utensils. The leaders of Israel, the heads of their ancestral houses, brought their offerings: six covered wagons and twelve oxen, a wagon for every two leaders and an ox for each. They presented these before the tabernacle. The LORD instructed Moses to accept these offerings and distribute them to the Levites according to their service. Moses gave two wagons and four oxen to the Gershonites, and four wagons and eight oxen to the Merarites, under the supervision of Ithamar, son of Aaron. The Kohathites received none because they carried the holy items on their shoulders.

The leaders brought their offerings for the dedication of the altar when it was anointed. Each leader presented his offering on a specific day. On the first day, Nahshon, son of Amminadab, from the tribe of Judah, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the second day, Nethanel, son of Zuar, leader of Issachar, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the third day, Eliab, son of Helon, leader of Zebulun, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the fourth day, Elizur, son of Shedeur, leader of Reuben, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the fifth day, Shelumiel, son of Zurishaddai, leader of Simeon, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the sixth day, Eliasaph, son of Deuel, leader of Gad, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the seventh day, Elishama, son of Ammihud, leader of Ephraim, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the eighth day, Gamaliel, son of Pedahzur, leader of Manasseh, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.On the ninth day, Abidan, son of Gideoni, leader of the tribe of Benjamin, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the tenth day, Ahiezer, son of Ammishaddai, leader of the tribe of Dan, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the eleventh day, Pagiel, son of Ochran, leader of the tribe of Asher, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

On the twelfth day, Ahira, son of Enan, leader of the tribe of Naphtali, brought his offering: a silver dish weighing 130 shekels, a silver basin weighing 70 shekels, both filled with fine flour mixed with oil for a grain offering; a golden pan weighing 10 shekels filled with incense; a young bull, a ram, and a year-old male lamb for a burnt offering; a male goat for a sin offering; and for the peace offering, two oxen, five rams, five male goats, and five year-old male lambs.

These were the offerings for the dedication of the altar when it was anointed, brought by the leaders of Israel: twelve silver dishes, twelve silver basins, and twelve golden pans. Each silver dish weighed 130 shekels, and each basin weighed 70 shekels, making a total of 2,400 shekels of silver. The twelve golden pans, filled with incense, each weighed 10 shekels, totaling 120 shekels of gold. The offerings included twelve young bulls, twelve rams, and twelve year-old male lambs for burnt offerings, along with their grain offerings. For sin offerings, there were twelve male goats. For peace offerings, there were twenty-four oxen, sixty rams, sixty male goats, and sixty year-old male lambs. This was the dedication offering for the altar after it was anointed.

When Moses entered the tent of meeting to speak with the LORD, he heard the voice speaking to him from above the cover of the ark of the testimony, between the two cherubim, and the LORD spoke to him.

The LORD spoke to Moses, saying, "Speak to Aaron and tell him: When you set up the lamps, the seven lamps shall light the area in front of the lampstand." Aaron did so, setting up the lamps to light the area in front of the lampstand, as the LORD commanded Moses.

The LORD also instructed Moses to take the Levites from among the Israelites and purify them. To purify them, sprinkle them with the water of purification, have them shave their entire bodies, wash their clothes, and cleanse themselves. Then, have them take a young bull with its grain offering of fine flour mixed with oil, and another young bull for a sin offering. Present the Levites before the tent of meeting and assemble the whole congregation of Israel. Present the Levites before the LORD, and the Israelites shall lay their hands on the Levites. Aaron shall offer the Levites before the LORD as a wave offering from the Israelites, so they may perform the service of the LORD. The Levites shall lay their hands on the heads of the bulls, and offer one for a sin offering and the other for a burnt offering to make atonement for the Levites. Set the Levites before Aaron and his sons and offer them as a wave offering to the LORD. This will separate the Levites from the Israelites, and the Levites will belong to the LORD. After this, the Levites will go in to perform the service of the tent of meeting, having been purified and offered as a wave offering.

The LORD said, "The Levites are wholly given to Me from among the Israelites. Instead of all the firstborn of the Israelites, I have taken the Levites for Myself. All the firstborn in Israel, both human and animal, are Mine. On the day I struck down all the firstborn in Egypt, I consecrated them for Myself. I have taken the Levites in place of all the firstborn of the Israelites. I have given the Levites to Aaron and his sons from among the Israelites to perform the service of the tent of meeting and to make atonement for the Israelites, so no plague will strike the Israelites when they approach the sanctuary."

Moses, Aaron, and the whole congregation of Israel did as the LORD commanded concerning the Levites. The Levites purified themselves, washed their clothes, and Aaron offered them as a wave offering before the LORD and made atonement for them. After that, the Levites went in to perform their service in the tent of meeting before Aaron and his sons, as the LORD had commanded Moses.

The LORD spoke to Moses in the wilderness of Sinai in the first month of the second year after they had come out of Egypt, saying, "Let the Israelites keep the Passover at its appointed time. On the fourteenth day of this month, at twilight, they shall keep it according to all its statutes and ordinances." Moses instructed the Israelites to keep the Passover, and they did so in the wilderness of Sinai on the fourteenth day of the first month, as the LORD commanded Moses.

The LORD also spoke to Moses about the Levites' service: "From twenty-five years old and upward, they shall enter to perform the service in the tent of meeting. At the age of fifty, they shall retire from the service and work no more, but they may assist their brothers in the tent of meeting to keep the charge, but they shall not do the work. This is how you shall manage the Levites' duties."

Some men were unclean because of contact with a dead body and could not keep the Passover on that day. They approached Moses and Aaron and asked why they should be kept from presenting the LORD's offering at its appointed time. Moses told them to wait while he listened to what the LORD would command concerning them. The LORD instructed Moses that if anyone is unclean due to a dead body or is on a journey, they may still keep the Passover in the second month on the fourteenth day at twilight. They shall eat it with unleavened bread and bitter herbs."Do not leave any of it until morning, and do not break any of its bones. Follow all the Passover regulations. 

If someone is clean and not on a journey but fails to observe the Passover, they must be cut off from their people because they did not present the LORD's offering at the appointed time. They will bear their sin. 

If a foreigner living among you wants to celebrate the Passover to the LORD, they must do so according to its regulations and rules. The same law applies to both the foreigner and the native-born.

On the day the tabernacle was set up, a cloud covered it, and at night it looked like fire. This continued: the cloud covered it by day, and the appearance of fire by night. Whenever the cloud lifted from the tent, the Israelites would set out, and wherever the cloud settled, the Israelites would camp. 

At the LORD's command, the Israelites set out, and at His command, they camped. As long as the cloud stayed over the tabernacle, they remained in camp. When the cloud stayed over the tabernacle for a long time, the Israelites obeyed the LORD's order and did not set out. Sometimes the cloud was over the tabernacle for only a few days; at the LORD's command, they would camp, and at His command, they would set out. Sometimes the cloud stayed only from evening until morning, and when it lifted in the morning, they set out. Whether by day or by night, whenever the cloud lifted, they set out. Whether it was two days, a month, or a year that the cloud remained over the tabernacle, the Israelites stayed in camp and did not set out; but when it lifted, they set out. At the LORD's command, they camped, and at the LORD's command, they set out. They obeyed the LORD's order, given through Moses.

In the second year, on the twentieth day of the second month, the cloud lifted from above the tabernacle of the testimony. The Israelites set out from the Desert of Sinai and traveled from place to place until the cloud came to rest in the Desert of Paran. They set out, this first time, at the LORD's command through Moses.

Moses said to Hobab, son of Reuel the Midianite, Moses' father-in-law, "We are setting out for the place the LORD promised to give us. Come with us, and we will treat you well, for the LORD has promised good things to Israel." But Hobab replied, "I will not go; I am going back to my own land and my own people." Moses said, "Please do not leave us. You know where we should camp in the desert, and you can be our eyes. If you come with us, we will share with you whatever good things the LORD gives us."

The LORD said to Moses, "Make two trumpets of hammered silver, and use them for calling the community together and for having the camps set out. When both are sounded, the whole community is to assemble before you at the entrance to the tent of meeting. If only one is sounded, the leaders—the heads of the clans of Israel—are to assemble before you. When a trumpet blast is sounded, the tribes camping on the east are to set out. At the sound of a second blast, the camps on the south are to set out. The blast will be the signal for setting out. To gather the assembly, blow the trumpets, but not with the signal for setting out. The sons of Aaron, the priests, are to blow the trumpets. This is to be a lasting ordinance for you and the generations to come. When you go into battle in your own land against an enemy who is oppressing you, sound a blast on the trumpets. Then you will be remembered by the LORD your God and rescued from your enemies. Also, at your times of rejoicing—your appointed festivals and New Moon feasts—you are to sound the trumpets over your burnt offerings and fellowship offerings, and they will be a memorial for you before your God. I am the LORD your God."

The Israelites set out from the mountain of the LORD and traveled for three days. The ark of the covenant of the LORD went before them during those three days to find them a place to rest. The cloud of the LORD was over them by day when they set out from the camp. Whenever the ark set out, Moses said, "Rise up, LORD! May your enemies be scattered; may your foes flee before you." Whenever it came to rest, he said, "Return, LORD, to the countless thousands of Israel."

The people complained about their hardships in the hearing of the LORD, and when He heard them, His anger was aroused. Then fire from the LORD burned among them and consumed some of the outskirts of the camp. When the people cried out to Moses, he prayed to the LORD, and the fire died down. So that place was called Taberah, because fire from the LORD had burned among them.

The LORD said to Moses, "Bring me seventy of Israel's elders who are known to you as leaders and officials among the people. Have them come to the tent of meeting, that they may stand there with you. I will come down and speak with you there, and I will take some of the power of the Spirit that is on you and put it on them. They will share the burden of the people with you so that you will not have to carry it alone."

Moses went out and told the people what the LORD had said. He brought together seventy of their elders and had them stand around the tent. Then the LORD came down in the cloud and spoke with him, and He took some of the power of the Spirit that was on him and put it on the seventy elders. When the Spirit rested on them, they prophesied—but did not do so again. However, two men, whose names were Eldad and Medad, had remained in the camp. They were listed among the elders but did not go out to the tent. Yet the Spirit also rested on them, and they prophesied in the camp. A young man ran and told Moses, "Eldad and Medad are prophesying in the camp." Joshua son of Nun, who had been Moses' aide since youth, spoke up and said, "Moses, my lord, stop them!" But Moses replied, "Are you jealous for my sake? I wish that all the LORD's people were prophets and that the LORD would put His Spirit on them!"

The mixed multitude among them began to crave other food, and again the Israelites started wailing and said, "If only we had meat to eat! We remember the fish we ate in Egypt at no cost—also the cucumbers, melons, leeks, onions, and garlic. But now we have lost our appetite; we never see anything but this manna!" The manna was like coriander seed and looked like resin. The people went around gathering it, and then ground it in a hand mill or crushed it in a mortar. They cooked it in a pot or made it into loaves. It tasted like something made with olive oil."The manna tasted like cakes baked with oil. When the dew fell on the camp at night, the manna fell with it. Moses heard the people weeping, each family at the entrance of their tent, and the LORD's anger was greatly kindled. Moses was also displeased.

The LORD instructed Moses to tell the people to prepare themselves, for they would eat meat the next day. They had complained, longing for the food they had in Egypt, so the LORD would give them meat to eat—not just for a day or two, but for a whole month, until they were sick of it. This was because they had rejected the LORD and complained about leaving Egypt.

Moses and the elders of Israel returned to the camp. A wind from the LORD brought quails from the sea, which fell around the camp, about a day's journey in every direction, and piled up about two cubits deep. The people gathered the quails all day, night, and the next day, collecting large amounts. They spread them out around the camp.

Moses questioned the LORD, feeling overwhelmed by the burden of leading the people. He asked why he had to carry the responsibility alone and expressed his inability to provide meat for everyone. The LORD reassured Moses, asking if His power was limited and promising that His word would come to pass.

While the people were still eating the meat, the LORD's anger was kindled, and He struck them with a severe plague. The place was named Kibroth-hattaavah, where they buried those who craved other food. From there, the people traveled to Hazeroth and stayed there.

Miriam and Aaron spoke against Moses because of the Cushite woman he had married. They questioned if the LORD had only spoken through Moses and not also through them. The LORD heard this and summoned Moses, Aaron, and Miriam to the tent of meeting. He came down in a pillar of cloud and called Aaron and Miriam forward. The LORD explained that He spoke to prophets through visions and dreams, but with Moses, He spoke face to face. The LORD's anger was kindled against them, and He departed. When the cloud lifted, Miriam was leprous, white as snow. Aaron pleaded with Moses not to hold their sin against them. Moses cried out to the LORD to heal her. The LORD instructed that Miriam be confined outside the camp for seven days, after which she was brought back, and the people continued their journey to the wilderness of Paran.

The LORD instructed Moses to send men to spy out the land of Canaan, one from each tribe. Moses sent them from the wilderness of Paran, and they explored the land from the wilderness of Zin to Rehob. They saw the descendants of Anak in Hebron and brought back a cluster of grapes, pomegranates, and figs from the valley of Eshcol. After forty days, they returned and reported to Moses, Aaron, and the congregation, showing them the fruit of the land. They confirmed that the land flowed with milk and honey but also reported that the inhabitants were strong and the cities fortified. Caleb urged the people to go up and possess the land, but the other spies spread a negative report, saying the land devoured its inhabitants and that they felt like grasshoppers compared to the giants there.

The congregation wept and murmured against Moses and Aaron, expressing a desire to return to Egypt. They questioned why the LORD had brought them to this land to die by the sword and suggested appointing a leader to take them back to Egypt.Moses and Aaron fell on their faces before the entire assembly of the Israelites. Joshua, son of Nun, and Caleb, son of Jephunneh, who were among those who scouted the land, tore their clothes in distress. They addressed the congregation, saying, "The land we explored is very good. If the LORD is pleased with us, He will bring us into this land, a land flowing with milk and honey, and give it to us. Do not rebel against the LORD or fear the people of the land, for we will devour them. Their protection is gone, but the LORD is with us. Do not be afraid of them."

However, the whole assembly talked about stoning them. Then the glory of the LORD appeared at the tent of meeting to all the Israelites. The LORD said to Moses, "How long will these people treat me with contempt? How long will they refuse to believe in me, despite all the signs I have performed among them? I will strike them down with a plague and destroy them, but I will make you into a nation greater and stronger than they."

Moses replied to the LORD, "Then the Egyptians will hear about it! By your power, you brought these people up from among them. They will tell the inhabitants of this land about it. They have already heard that you, LORD, are with these people and that you, LORD, have been seen face to face, that your cloud stays over them, and that you go before them in a pillar of cloud by day and a pillar of fire by night. If you put all these people to death, leaving none alive, the nations who have heard this report about you will say, 'The LORD was not able to bring these people into the land he promised them on oath, so he slaughtered them in the wilderness.'

"Now may the Lord's strength be displayed, just as you have declared: 'The LORD is slow to anger, abounding in love and forgiving sin and rebellion. Yet he does not leave the guilty unpunished; he punishes the children for the sin of the parents to the third and fourth generation.' In accordance with your great love, forgive the sin of these people, just as you have pardoned them from the time they left Egypt until now."

The LORD replied, "I have forgiven them, as you asked. Nevertheless, as surely as I live and as surely as the glory of the LORD fills the whole earth, not one of those who saw my glory and the signs I performed in Egypt and in the wilderness but who disobeyed me and tested me ten times—not one of them will ever see the land I promised on oath to their ancestors. No one who has treated me with contempt will ever see it. But because my servant Caleb has a different spirit and follows me wholeheartedly, I will bring him into the land he went to, and his descendants will inherit it. Since the Amalekites and the Canaanites are living in the valleys, turn back tomorrow and set out toward the desert along the route to the Red Sea."

The LORD said to Moses and Aaron, "How long will this wicked community grumble against me? I have heard the complaints of these grumbling Israelites. So tell them, 'As surely as I live, declares the LORD, I will do to you the very thing I heard you say: In this wilderness, your bodies will fall—every one of you twenty years old or more who was counted in the census and who has grumbled against me. Not one of you will enter the land I swore with uplifted hand to make your home, except Caleb son of Jephunneh and Joshua son of Nun. As for your children that you said would be taken as plunder, I will bring them in to enjoy the land you have rejected. But as for you, your bodies will fall in this wilderness. Your children will be shepherds here for forty years, suffering for your unfaithfulness, until the last of your bodies lies in the wilderness. For forty years—one year for each of the forty days you explored the land—you will suffer for your sins and know what it is like to have me against you.' I, the LORD, have spoken, and I will surely do these things to this whole wicked community, which has banded together against me. They will meet their end in this wilderness; here they will die."

So the men Moses had sent to explore the land, who returned and made the whole community grumble against him by spreading a bad report about it—these men who were responsible for spreading the bad report about the land were struck down and died of a plague before the LORD. Of the men who went to explore the land, only Joshua son of Nun and Caleb son of Jephunneh survived.

When Moses reported this to all the Israelites, they mourned bitterly. Early the next morning, they set out for the highest point in the hill country, saying, "Now we are ready to go up to the land the LORD promised. Surely we have sinned!"

But Moses said, "Why are you disobeying the LORD's command? This will not succeed! Do not go up, because the LORD is not with you. You will be defeated by your enemies, for the Amalekites and the Canaanites will face you there. Because you have turned away from the LORD, he will not be with you, and you will fall by the sword."

Nevertheless, in their presumption, they went up toward the highest point in the hill country, though neither Moses nor the ark of the LORD's covenant moved from the camp.
