The LORD commanded us to obey all these decrees and to fear the LORD our God, so that we might always prosper and be kept alive, as is the case today. And if we are careful to obey all this law before the LORD our God, as He has commanded us, that will be our righteousness.'

When the LORD your God brings you into the land you are entering to possess and drives out before you many nations—the Hittites, Girgashites, Amorites, Canaanites, Perizzites, Hivites, and Jebusites, seven nations larger and stronger than you—and when the LORD your God has delivered them over to you and you have defeated them, then you must destroy them totally. Make no treaty with them and show them no mercy. Do not intermarry with them. Do not give your daughters to their sons or take their daughters for your sons, for they will turn your children away from following me to serve other gods, and the LORD's anger will burn against you and will quickly destroy you. This is what you are to do to them: Break down their altars, smash their sacred stones, cut down their Asherah poles, and burn their idols in the fire.

For you are a people holy to the LORD your God. The LORD your God has chosen you out of all the peoples on the face of the earth to be His people, His treasured possession. The LORD did not set His affection on you and choose you because you were more numerous than other peoples, for you were the fewest of all peoples. But it was because the LORD loved you and kept the oath He swore to your ancestors that He brought you out with a mighty hand and redeemed you from the land of slavery, from the power of Pharaoh king of Egypt. Know therefore that the LORD your God is God; He is the faithful God, keeping His covenant of love to a thousand generations of those who love Him and keep His commandments. But those who hate Him, He will repay to their face by destruction; He will not be slow to repay to their face those who hate Him.

Therefore, take care to follow the commands, decrees, and laws I give you today. If you pay attention to these laws and are careful to follow them, then the LORD your God will keep His covenant of love with you, as He swore to your ancestors. He will love you and bless you and increase your numbers. He will bless the fruit of your womb, the crops of your land—your grain, new wine, and olive oil—the calves of your herds and the lambs of your flocks in the land He swore to your ancestors to give you. You will be blessed more than any other people; none of your men or women will be childless, nor will any of your livestock be without young. The LORD will keep you free from every disease. He will not inflict on you the horrible diseases you knew in Egypt, but He will inflict them on all who hate you."When the LORD your God brings you into the land He promised to your ancestors, He will drive out many nations before you. These nations are larger and stronger than you, but do not be afraid. Remember what the LORD did to Pharaoh and all of Egypt. The same signs, wonders, and mighty acts will be done to these nations. The LORD will send hornets to drive them out until they are destroyed. Do not fear them, for the LORD your God is with you, a great and awesome God.

The LORD will gradually drive out these nations before you, so the wild animals do not become too numerous. He will deliver their kings into your hands, and you will wipe out their names from under heaven. No one will be able to stand against you until you have destroyed them. Do not serve their gods, for that will be a trap for you. Burn their idols and do not covet the silver or gold on them, for it is detestable to the LORD. Do not bring any detestable thing into your house, or you will be set apart for destruction like it. Utterly detest and abhor it, for it is set apart for destruction.

Be careful to follow all the commands I give you today, so you may live and increase and enter the land the LORD promised to your ancestors. Remember how the LORD led you through the wilderness for forty years, humbling and testing you to know what was in your heart. He humbled you, causing you to hunger and then feeding you with manna, to teach you that man does not live on bread alone but on every word that comes from the mouth of the LORD. Your clothes did not wear out, and your feet did not swell during these forty years.

When you have eaten and are satisfied, and have built fine houses and settled down, and when your herds and flocks grow large and your silver and gold increase, do not become proud and forget the LORD your God who brought you out of Egypt, out of the land of slavery. He led you through the vast and dreadful wilderness, with its venomous snakes and scorpions, and brought you water out of hard rock. He gave you manna to eat in the wilderness to humble and test you so that in the end it might go well with you. You may say to yourself, "My power and the strength of my hands have produced this wealth for me." But remember the LORD your God, for it is He who gives you the ability to produce wealth, confirming His covenant.

If you ever forget the LORD your God and follow other gods, worshiping and bowing down to them, you will surely be destroyed. Like the nations the LORD destroyed before you, so you will be destroyed for not obeying the LORD your God.

Listen, Israel: You are about to cross the Jordan to dispossess nations greater and stronger than you, with large cities that have walls up to the sky. The people are strong and tall, descendants of the Anakim. But know that the LORD your God goes before you as a consuming fire. He will destroy them and subdue them before you. Do not say in your heart, "The LORD has brought me here to take possession of this land because of my righteousness." It is not because of your righteousness but because of the wickedness of these nations that the LORD is driving them out. Understand that it is not because of your righteousness, for you are a stubborn people.

Remember how you provoked the LORD to anger in the wilderness. From the day you left Egypt until you arrived here, you have been rebellious. At Horeb, you made the LORD angry enough to destroy you. When I went up the mountain to receive the tablets of the covenant, I stayed forty days and nights without eating or drinking. The LORD gave me the two stone tablets inscribed by His finger. But when I came down, I saw that you had sinned against the LORD by making a molten calf. I broke the tablets and fell prostrate before the LORD for forty days and nights, pleading for you because of your sin.

The LORD was angry enough to destroy Aaron, but I prayed for him too. I took the calf you made, burned it, crushed it, and threw the dust into a stream. You have been rebellious against the LORD from the day I knew you. When the LORD sent you from Kadesh-barnea to possess the land, you rebelled and did not trust Him. I lay prostrate before the LORD for forty days and nights because He said He would destroy you. I prayed, "O Lord GOD, do not destroy Your people, Your inheritance, whom You redeemed by Your greatness and brought out of Egypt with a mighty hand. Remember Your servants, Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. Do not look at the stubbornness of this people or their wickedness and sin."When the LORD your God brings you into the land He promised to your ancestors, He will drive out many nations before you. These nations are larger and stronger than you, but do not be afraid. Remember what the LORD did to Pharaoh and all of Egypt. The same signs, wonders, and mighty acts will be done to these nations. The LORD will send hornets to drive them out until they are destroyed. Do not fear them, for the LORD your God is with you, a great and awesome God.

The LORD will gradually drive out these nations before you, so the wild animals do not become too numerous. He will deliver their kings into your hands, and you will wipe out their names from under heaven. No one will be able to stand against you until you have destroyed them. Do not serve their gods, for that will be a trap for you. Burn their idols and do not covet the silver or gold on them, for it is detestable to the LORD. Do not bring any detestable thing into your house, or you will be set apart for destruction like it. Utterly detest and abhor it, for it is set apart for destruction.

Be careful to follow all the commands I give you today, so you may live and increase and enter the land the LORD promised to your ancestors. Remember how the LORD led you through the wilderness for forty years, humbling and testing you to know what was in your heart. He humbled you, causing you to hunger and then feeding you with manna, to teach you that man does not live on bread alone but on every word that comes from the mouth of the LORD. Your clothes did not wear out, and your feet did not swell during these forty years.

When you have eaten and are satisfied, and have built fine houses and settled down, and when your herds and flocks grow large and your silver and gold increase, do not become proud and forget the LORD your God who brought you out of Egypt, out of the land of slavery. He led you through the vast and dreadful wilderness, with its venomous snakes and scorpions, and brought you water out of hard rock. He gave you manna to eat in the wilderness to humble and test you so that in the end it might go well with you. You may say to yourself, "My power and the strength of my hands have produced this wealth for me." But remember the LORD your God, for it is He who gives you the ability to produce wealth, confirming His covenant.

If you ever forget the LORD your God and follow other gods, worshiping and bowing down to them, you will surely be destroyed. Like the nations the LORD destroyed before you, so you will be destroyed for not obeying the LORD your God.

Listen, Israel: You are about to cross the Jordan to dispossess nations greater and stronger than you, with large cities that have walls up to the sky. The people are strong and tall, descendants of the Anakim. But know that the LORD your God goes before you as a consuming fire. He will destroy them and subdue them before you. Do not say in your heart, "The LORD has brought me here to take possession of this land because of my righteousness." It is not because of your righteousness but because of the wickedness of these nations that the LORD is driving them out. Understand that it is not because of your righteousness, for you are a stubborn people.

Remember how you provoked the LORD to anger in the wilderness. From the day you left Egypt until you arrived here, you have been rebellious. At Horeb, you made the LORD angry enough to destroy you. When I went up the mountain to receive the tablets of the covenant, I stayed forty days and nights without eating or drinking. The LORD gave me the two stone tablets inscribed by His finger. But when I came down, I saw that you had sinned against the LORD by making a molten calf. I broke the tablets and fell prostrate before the LORD for forty days and nights, pleading for you because of your sin.

The LORD was angry enough to destroy Aaron, but I prayed for him too. I took the calf you made, burned it, crushed it, and threw the dust into a stream. You have been rebellious against the LORD from the day I knew you. When the LORD sent you from Kadesh-barnea to possess the land, you rebelled and did not trust Him. I lay prostrate before the LORD for forty days and nights because He said He would destroy you. I prayed, "O Lord GOD, do not destroy Your people, Your inheritance, whom You redeemed by Your greatness and brought out of Egypt with a mighty hand. Remember Your servants, Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob. Do not look at the stubbornness of this people or their wickedness and sin."

They might say, "Because the LORD was not able to bring them into the land He promised them, and because He hated them, He brought them out to kill them in the wilderness." But they are Your people and Your inheritance, whom You brought out by Your great power and Your outstretched arm.

The Israelites traveled from Beeroth-benejaakan to Moserah; there Aaron died and was buried, and his son Eleazar succeeded him as priest. At that time, the LORD said to me, "Chisel out two stone tablets like the first ones and come up to Me on the mountain. Also, make a wooden ark. I will write on the tablets the words that were on the first tablets, which you broke. Then you shall put them in the ark." So I made an ark out of acacia wood and chiseled out two stone tablets like the first ones. I went up the mountain with the two tablets in my hands. The LORD wrote on these tablets what He had written before, the Ten Commandments He had spoken to you on the mountain out of the fire on the day of the assembly. Then I came back down the mountain and put the tablets in the ark I had made, as the LORD commanded me, and they are there now.

From there, the Israelites traveled to Gudgodah and then to Jotbathah, a land with streams of water. At that time, the LORD set apart the tribe of Levi to carry the ark of the covenant of the LORD, to stand before the LORD to minister, and to pronounce blessings in His name, as they still do today. That is why the Levites have no share or inheritance among their fellow Israelites; the LORD is their inheritance, as the LORD your God told them.

I stayed on the mountain for forty days and nights, as I did the first time, and the LORD listened to me again. He did not want to destroy you. The LORD said to me, "Go and lead the people on their way, so they may enter and possess the land I swore to their ancestors to give them."

And now, Israel, what does the LORD your God ask of you but to fear the LORD your God, to walk in obedience to Him, to love Him, to serve the LORD your God with all your heart and with all your soul, and to observe the LORD's commands and decrees that I am giving you today for your own good? To the LORD your God belong the heavens, even the highest heavens, the earth and everything in it. Yet the LORD set His affection on your ancestors and loved them, and He chose you, their descendants, above all the nations, as it is today. Circumcise your hearts, therefore, and do not be stiff-necked any longer. For the LORD your God is God of gods and Lord of lords, the great God, mighty and awesome, who shows no partiality and accepts no bribes. He defends the cause of the fatherless and the widow, and loves the foreigner residing among you, giving them food and clothing. And you are to love those who are foreigners, for you yourselves were foreigners in Egypt. Fear the LORD your God and serve Him. Hold fast to Him and take your oaths in His name. He is the one you praise; He is your God, who performed for you those great and awesome wonders you saw with your own eyes. Your ancestors who went down into Egypt were seventy in all, and now the LORD your God has made you as numerous as the stars in the sky.

Love the LORD your God and keep His requirements, His decrees, His laws, and His commands always. Remember today that your children were not the ones who saw and experienced the discipline of the LORD your God: His majesty, His mighty hand, His outstretched arm; the signs He performed and the things He did in the heart of Egypt, both to Pharaoh king of Egypt and to his whole country; what He did to the Egyptian army, to its horses and chariots, how He overwhelmed them with the waters of the Red Sea as they pursued you, and how the LORD brought lasting ruin on them. It was not your children who saw what He did for you in the wilderness until you arrived at this place, and what He did to Dathan and Abiram, sons of Eliab the Reubenite, when the earth opened its mouth right in the middle of all Israel and swallowed them up with their households, their tents, and every living thing that belonged to them. But it was your own eyes that saw all these great things the LORD has done.

Observe therefore all the commands I am giving you today, so that you may have the strength to go in and take over the land that you are crossing the Jordan to possess, and so that you may live long in the land the LORD swore to your ancestors to give to them and their descendants, a land flowing with milk and honey. The land you are entering to take over is not like the land of Egypt, from which you have come, where you planted your seed and irrigated it by foot as in a vegetable garden. But the land you are crossing the Jordan to take possession of is a land of mountains and valleys that drinks rain from heaven. It is a land the LORD your God cares for; the eyes of the LORD your God are continually on it from the beginning of the year to its end.

So if you faithfully obey the commands I am giving you today—to love the LORD your God and to serve Him with all your heart and with all your soul—then I will send rain on your land in its season, both autumn and spring rains, so that you may gather in your grain, new wine, and olive oil. I will provide grass in the fields for your cattle, and you will eat and be satisfied. Be careful, or you will be enticed to turn away and worship other gods and bow down to them. Then the LORD's anger will burn against you, and He will shut up the heavens so that it will not rain and the ground will yield no produce, and you will soon perish from the good land the LORD is giving you.

Fix these words of mine in your hearts and minds; tie them as symbols on your hands and bind them on your foreheads. Teach them to your children, talking about them when you sit at home and when you walk along the road, when you lie down and when you get up. Write them on the doorframes of your houses and on your gates, so that your days and the days of your children may be many in the land the LORD swore to give your ancestors, as many as the days that the heavens are above the earth.

If you carefully observe all these commands I am giving you to follow—to love the LORD your God, to walk in obedience to Him and to hold fast to Him—then the LORD will drive out all these nations before you, and you will dispossess nations larger and stronger than you. Every place where you set your foot will be yours: Your territory will extend from the desert to Lebanon, and from the Euphrates River to the Mediterranean Sea. No one will be able to stand against you. The LORD your God, as He promised you, will put the terror and fear of you on the whole land, wherever you go.

See, I am setting before you today a blessing and a curse—the blessing if you obey the commands of the LORD your God that I am giving you today; the curse if you disobey the commands of the LORD your God and turn from the way that I command you today by following other gods, which you have not known. When the LORD your God has brought you into the land you are entering to possess, you are to proclaim the blessings on Mount Gerizim and the curses on Mount Ebal. As you know, these mountains are across the Jordan, west of the road, toward the setting sun, near the great trees of Moreh, in the territory of those Canaanites living in the Arabah in the vicinity of Gilgal. You are about to cross the Jordan to enter and take possession of the land the LORD your God is giving you. When you have taken it over and are living there, be sure that you obey all the decrees and laws I am setting before you today."Hold fast to Him and swear by His name. He is your glory and your God, who has done these great and awesome things that you have seen with your own eyes. Your ancestors went down to Egypt with seventy people, and now the LORD your God has made you as numerous as the stars in the sky.

Love the LORD your God and always keep His requirements, decrees, laws, and commands. Remember today that it was not your children who saw and experienced the discipline of the LORD your God—His greatness, His mighty hand, His outstretched arm, the signs He performed, and the things He did in Egypt to Pharaoh and his entire country. They did not see what He did to the Egyptian army, their horses, and chariots, how He overwhelmed them with the waters of the Red Sea as they pursued you, and how the LORD brought lasting ruin on them. They did not see what He did for you in the wilderness until you arrived at this place, or what He did to Dathan and Abiram, sons of Eliab the Reubenite, when the earth opened its mouth and swallowed them, their households, tents, and every living thing that belonged to them. But it was your own eyes that saw all these great things the LORD has done.

Therefore, observe all the commands I am giving you today, so that you may have the strength to go in and take over the land you are crossing the Jordan to possess, and so that you may live long in the land the LORD swore to give to your ancestors and their descendants, a land flowing with milk and honey. The land you are entering to take over is not like the land of Egypt, from which you came, where you planted your seed and irrigated it by foot as in a vegetable garden. But the land you are crossing the Jordan to take possession of is a land of mountains and valleys that drinks rain from heaven. It is a land the LORD your God cares for; the eyes of the LORD your God are continually on it from the beginning of the year to its end.

If you faithfully obey the commands I am giving you today—to love the LORD your God and to serve Him with all your heart and with all your soul—then I will send rain on your land in its season, both autumn and spring rains, so that you may gather in your grain, new wine, and olive oil. I will provide grass in the fields for your cattle, and you will eat and be satisfied. Be careful, or you will be enticed to turn away and worship other gods and bow down to them. Then the LORD's anger will burn against you, and He will shut up the heavens so that it will not rain and the ground will yield no produce, and you will soon perish from the good land the LORD is giving you.

Fix these words of mine in your hearts and minds; tie them as symbols on your hands and bind them on your foreheads. Teach them to your children, talking about them when you sit at home and when you walk along the road, when you lie down and when you get up. Write them on the doorframes of your houses and on your gates, so that your days and the days of your children may be many in the land the LORD swore to give your ancestors, as many as the days that the heavens are above the earth.

If you carefully observe all these commands I am giving you to follow—to love the LORD your God, to walk in obedience to Him and to hold fast to Him—then the LORD will drive out all these nations before you, and you will dispossess nations larger and stronger than you. Every place where you set your foot will be yours: Your territory will extend from the desert to Lebanon, and from the Euphrates River to the Mediterranean Sea. No one will be able to stand against you. The LORD your God, as He promised you, will put the terror and fear of you on the whole land, wherever you go.

See, I am setting before you today a blessing and a curse—the blessing if you obey the commands of the LORD your God that I am giving you today; the curse if you disobey the commands of the LORD your God and turn from the way that I command you today by following other gods, which you have not known. When the LORD your God has brought you into the land you are entering to possess, you are to proclaim the blessings on Mount Gerizim and the curses on Mount Ebal. As you know, these mountains are across the Jordan, west of the road, toward the setting sun, near the great trees of Moreh, in the territory of those Canaanites living in the Arabah in the vicinity of Gilgal. You are about to cross the Jordan to enter and take possession of the land the LORD your God is giving you. When you have taken it over and are living there, be sure that you obey all the decrees and laws I am setting before you today."Do not follow the gods of the people around you, whether they are near or far. If someone tries to lead you to worship other gods, do not listen to them or show them any mercy. You must be the first to act against them, and then all the people should join in. Stone them to death because they tried to turn you away from the LORD your God, who freed you from Egypt. This will serve as a warning to all of Israel to prevent such wickedness.

Be careful not to offer your burnt offerings just anywhere. Offer them only at the place the LORD chooses among your tribes. If you hear that some people in one of your cities are leading others to worship other gods, investigate thoroughly. If it is true, destroy that city completely, including its livestock, and burn all its spoils as an offering to the LORD. The city must remain a ruin forever. Do not keep any of the spoils for yourself, so that the LORD may turn from His anger and show you mercy, as He promised your ancestors.

You may eat meat within your gates, as long as it is not the blood, which must be poured out on the ground. You are a holy people to the LORD, so do not eat anything that dies of itself. You may give it to a foreigner or sell it to a stranger. Do not cook a young goat in its mother's milk.

You must bring a tithe of your crops each year to the place the LORD chooses. If the place is too far, convert your tithe into money and spend it on whatever you desire when you get there. Eat and rejoice before the LORD with your household and do not neglect the Levites.

Every three years, bring all your tithes to your gates so that the Levites, foreigners, orphans, and widows can eat and be satisfied. This will ensure the LORD's blessing on all your work.

Sanctify the firstborn males of your herd and flock to the LORD. Eat them yearly at the place the LORD chooses. If they have any defects, do not sacrifice them but eat them within your gates. Do not eat the blood; pour it out on the ground.

Every seven years, cancel debts. Creditors must release what they have lent to their neighbors and fellow Israelites because the LORD's release has been proclaimed. You may collect from foreigners, but not from your fellow Israelites. There should be no needy among you, for the LORD will bless you in the land He is giving you.Listen carefully to the voice of the LORD your God and follow all the commandments I give you today. The LORD will bless you as promised, and you will lend to many nations but not borrow; you will rule over many nations, but they will not rule over you.

Observe the month of Abib and celebrate Passover to the LORD your God, for it was in this month that the LORD brought you out of Egypt by night. Sacrifice the Passover offering from your flock and herd at the place the LORD chooses. Eat unleavened bread for seven days, the bread of affliction, to remember your hurried departure from Egypt. No leaven should be seen in your territory for seven days, and none of the meat from the sacrifice should remain until morning.

You must not sacrifice the Passover offering within any of your gates but at the place the LORD chooses. Roast and eat it there, then return to your tents in the morning. For six days, eat unleavened bread, and on the seventh day, hold a solemn assembly to the LORD and do no work.

If there is a needy person among you, do not harden your heart or close your hand. Open your hand and lend whatever is needed. Do not be stingy because the seventh year, the year of release, is near. Give generously without a grudging heart, and the LORD will bless you in all your work. The poor will always be in the land, so be open-handed toward your fellow Israelites who are poor and needy.

Count seven weeks from when you begin to harvest the grain, then celebrate the Feast of Weeks to the LORD with a freewill offering. Rejoice before the LORD with your family, servants, the Levites, foreigners, orphans, and widows at the place the LORD chooses. Remember that you were slaves in Egypt and follow these decrees.

If a fellow Hebrew, man or woman, sells themselves to you, they shall serve for six years, and in the seventh year, you must set them free. When you release them, do not send them away empty-handed. Provide generously from your flock, threshing floor, and winepress, as the LORD has blessed you. Remember that you were slaves in Egypt, and the LORD redeemed you. If the servant chooses to stay because they love you and your household, pierce their ear with an awl, and they will become your servant for life. Do the same for your female servants. Do not consider it a hardship to set them free, for they have served you well, and the LORD will bless you in all you do.

Celebrate the Feast of Tabernacles for seven days after gathering your harvest. Rejoice with your family, servants, the Levites, foreigners, orphans, and widows at the place the LORD chooses. The LORD will bless your harvest and all your work, and you will be joyful. Three times a year, all your males must appear before the LORD at the place He chooses: the Feast of Unleavened Bread, the Feast of Weeks, and the Feast of Tabernacles. Do not appear before the LORD empty-handed; each person should give as they are able, according to the blessings the LORD has given them.

Appoint judges and officers in all your towns that the LORD gives you, and they shall judge the people fairly. Do not pervert justice or show partiality. Do not accept bribes, for they blind the eyes of the wise and twist the words of the righteous. Follow justice and live, and you will inherit the land the LORD gives you.

When you enter the land the LORD gives you and take possession of it, you may say, "Let us set a king over us like the other nations." Be sure to appoint the king the LORD chooses, one from among your fellow Israelites. Do not place a foreigner over you. The king must not acquire many horses or return the people to Egypt to get more horses. He must not take many wives or accumulate large amounts of silver and gold. When he takes the throne, he must write a copy of this law and read it all his life to learn to fear the LORD and follow His laws. This will keep him humble and ensure a long reign for him and his descendants.

Do not plant an Asherah pole or set up a sacred stone beside the altar of the LORD. The priests, the Levites, shall have no inheritance among the Israelites; they will live on the offerings made to the LORD. The firstfruits of your grain, wine, oil, and wool should be given to them, for the LORD has chosen them to minister in His name. If a Levite moves to the place the LORD chooses, he may serve there like his fellow Levites and share in the offerings.

Do not sacrifice an ox or sheep with any defect, for that is detestable to the LORD. If someone is found worshiping other gods, investigate thoroughly. If it is true, bring that person to the city gates and stone them to death.If a man or woman is found guilty of doing something evil, bring them to the city gates and stone them to death. A person can only be put to death on the testimony of two or three witnesses, not just one. The witnesses must be the first to throw stones, followed by the rest of the people, to remove the evil from among you.

When you enter the land the LORD your God is giving you, do not adopt the detestable practices of the nations there. Do not sacrifice your children in fire, practice divination, sorcery, witchcraft, cast spells, or consult spirits. These practices are detestable to the LORD, and because of them, He is driving out those nations before you. Be wholehearted with the LORD your God. The nations you will dispossess listen to those who practice sorcery and divination, but the LORD your God has not permitted you to do so.

If a legal matter is too difficult for you to judge, such as cases of bloodshed, lawsuits, or assaults, go to the place the LORD your God will choose. Consult the Levitical priests and the judge in office at that time. They will give you a verdict, and you must act according to their decision. Follow their instructions carefully and do not turn aside from what they tell you.

The LORD your God will raise up for you a prophet like me from among your fellow Israelites. You must listen to him. This is what you asked of the LORD your God at Horeb on the day of the assembly when you said, "Let us not hear the voice of the LORD our God nor see this great fire anymore, or we will die." The LORD said to me, "What they say is good. I will raise up for them a prophet like you from among their fellow Israelites, and I will put my words in his mouth. He will tell them everything I command him. Anyone who does not listen to my words that the prophet speaks in my name, I will call to account."

If a prophet presumes to speak in my name anything I have not commanded, or speaks in the name of other gods, that prophet must be put to death. You may wonder, "How can we know when a message has not been spoken by the LORD?" If what a prophet proclaims in the name of the LORD does not take place or come true, that is a message the LORD has not spoken. The prophet has spoken presumptuously, so do not be alarmed.

When the LORD your God has destroyed the nations whose land He is giving you, and you have taken possession of their cities and houses, set aside three cities in the land the LORD your God is giving you to possess. Prepare roads to these cities and divide the land into three parts so that anyone who kills someone unintentionally may flee there.

When you go to war against your enemies and see horses and chariots and an army greater than yours, do not be afraid, for the LORD your God, who brought you out of Egypt, will be with you. Before the battle, the priest shall come forward and address the army, saying, "Hear, O Israel, today you are going into battle against your enemies. Do not be fainthearted or afraid; do not panic or be terrified by them. For the LORD your God is the one who goes with you to fight for you against your enemies to give you victory."

If a man has built a new house and has not yet dedicated it, let him go home, or he may die in battle and someone else will dedicate it. If a man has planted a vineyard and has not yet begun to enjoy its fruit, let him go home, or he may die in battle and someone else will enjoy it. If a man has become engaged to a woman and has not married her, let him go home, or he may die in battle and someone else will marry her. If anyone is afraid or fainthearted, let him go home so that his fellow soldiers will not become disheartened too.

When you approach a city to fight against it, offer it terms of peace. If it accepts and opens its gates, all the people in it shall become your forced labor and serve you. If it refuses to make peace and engages you in battle, lay siege to the city. When the LORD your God delivers it into your hand, put all the men to the sword. But take the women, children, livestock, and everything else in the city as plunder for yourselves. Use the plunder the LORD your God gives you from your enemies.

Do not destroy the trees by putting an axe to them, for you can eat their fruit. Do not cut them down. Are the trees people, that you should besiege them? Only cut down trees that you know are not fruit trees to build siege works against the city that is at war with you until it falls.

A single witness is not enough to convict someone of any crime or offense they may have committed. A matter must be established by the testimony of two or three witnesses. If a malicious witness takes the stand to accuse someone of a crime, the two people involved in the dispute must stand in the presence of the LORD before the priests and the judges who are in office at the time. The judges must make a thorough investigation, and if the witness proves to be a liar, giving false testimony against a fellow Israelite, then do to the false witness as that witness intended to do to the other party. You must purge the evil from among you. The rest of the people will hear of this and be afraid, and never again will such an evil thing be done among you. Show no pity: life for life, eye for eye, tooth for tooth, hand for hand, foot for foot.If someone is found murdered in the land the LORD your God is giving you, and it is unknown who killed them, the elders and judges must come forward and measure the distance to the surrounding cities. The elders of the nearest city must take a heifer that has never been worked or yoked, bring it to a valley that has not been plowed or sown, and break its neck there. The Levitical priests, chosen by the LORD to serve Him and pronounce blessings, will oversee the matter. The elders of the city will wash their hands over the heifer and declare, "Our hands did not shed this blood, nor did our eyes see it. Forgive your people Israel, whom you have redeemed, and do not hold the guilt of innocent blood against them." This will absolve them of the bloodshed.

When you go to war and the LORD your God delivers your enemies into your hands, and you take captives, if you see a beautiful woman among them and desire her as your wife, bring her into your home. She must shave her head, trim her nails, and remove her captive's clothes. She will stay in your house and mourn her parents for a month. After that, you may marry her. If you are not pleased with her, you must let her go free and not sell her or treat her as a slave, since you have humiliated her.

If a man has two wives, one loved and the other unloved, and both bear him sons, but the firstborn is the son of the unloved wife, he must acknowledge the firstborn by giving him a double portion of his inheritance. The right of the firstborn belongs to him.

If a man has a stubborn and rebellious son who does not obey his parents even after they discipline him, his parents must bring him to the city elders at the gate and say, "This son of ours is stubborn and rebellious. He will not obey us. He is a glutton and a drunkard." Then all the men of the city must stone him to death. This will remove the evil from among you, and all Israel will hear and be afraid.

A man who is hanged on a tree for a sin deserving death must not be left hanging overnight. You must bury him that same day, for anyone who is hanged is under God's curse. This will prevent defiling the land the LORD your God is giving you as an inheritance.If someone is found murdered in the land the LORD your God is giving you, and it is unknown who killed them, the elders and judges must come forward and measure the distance to the surrounding cities. The elders of the nearest city must take a heifer that has never been worked or yoked, bring it to a valley that has not been plowed or sown, and break its neck there. The Levitical priests, chosen by the LORD to serve Him and pronounce blessings, will oversee the matter. The elders of the city will wash their hands over the heifer and declare, "Our hands did not shed this blood, nor did our eyes see it. Forgive your people Israel, whom you have redeemed, and do not hold the guilt of innocent blood against them." This will absolve them of the bloodshed.

When you go to war and the LORD your God delivers your enemies into your hands, and you take captives, if you see a beautiful woman among them and desire her as your wife, bring her into your home. She must shave her head, trim her nails, and remove her captive's clothes. She will stay in your house and mourn her parents for a month. After that, you may marry her. If you are not pleased with her, you must let her go free and not sell her or treat her as a slave, since you have humiliated her.

If a man has two wives, one loved and the other unloved, and both bear him sons, but the firstborn is the son of the unloved wife, he must acknowledge the firstborn by giving him a double portion of his inheritance. The right of the firstborn belongs to him.

If a man has a stubborn and rebellious son who does not obey his parents even after they discipline him, his parents must bring him to the city elders at the gate and say, "This son of ours is stubborn and rebellious. He will not obey us. He is a glutton and a drunkard." Then all the men of the city must stone him to death. This will remove the evil from among you, and all Israel will hear and be afraid.

A man who is hanged on a tree for a sin deserving death must not be left hanging overnight. You must bury him that same day, for anyone who is hanged is under God's curse. This will prevent defiling the land the LORD your God is giving you as an inheritance.

When you set up camp against your enemies, keep away from anything impure. If a man becomes unclean due to a nocturnal emission, he must go outside the camp and stay there. In the evening, he should bathe himself, and at sunset, he may return to the camp. Designate a place outside the camp where you can go to relieve yourself. Carry a tool with your equipment, and when you relieve yourself, dig a hole and cover your excrement. The LORD your God moves about in your camp to protect you and deliver your enemies to you. Your camp must be holy so that He will not see anything indecent among you and turn away from you.

Be careful with cases of leprosy; follow all the instructions given by the Levitical priests. Remember what the LORD your God did to Miriam on your way out of Egypt.

If you see your brother's ox or sheep straying, do not ignore it. Return it to your brother. If your brother is not nearby or you do not know who he is, take the animal home with you and keep it until your brother comes looking for it. Then return it to him. Do the same with his donkey, garment, or any lost item you find. Do not ignore it.

Do not hand over a slave who has escaped from his master to you. Let him live among you wherever he chooses, in any of your towns. Do not oppress him.

When you lend something to your neighbor, do not go into his house to get the pledge. Wait outside, and let the person to whom you are lending bring the pledge out to you. If the person is poor, do not keep the pledge overnight. Return it by sunset so that he may sleep in his cloak and bless you. This will be considered a righteous act before the LORD your God.

Do not see your brother's donkey or ox fallen on the road and ignore it. Help him lift it up.

There should be no prostitutes among the daughters of Israel or sodomites among the sons of Israel. Do not bring the earnings of a prostitute or the price of a dog into the house of the LORD your God for any vow, for both are detestable to the LORD your God.

Do not oppress a hired worker who is poor and needy, whether he is a fellow Israelite or a foreigner living in your towns. Pay him his wages each day before sunset because he is poor and depends on them. Otherwise, he may cry out to the LORD against you, and you will be guilty of sin.

A woman must not wear men's clothing, nor should a man wear women's clothing, for the LORD your God detests anyone who does this.

Do not charge interest on loans to your fellow Israelites, whether on money, food, or anything else that may earn interest. You may charge a foreigner interest, but not a fellow Israelite, so that the LORD your God may bless you in everything you do in the land you are entering to possess.

Parents are not to be put to death for their children, nor children for their parents; each will die for their own sin.

If you come across a bird's nest with chicks or eggs, and the mother is sitting on them, do not take the mother with the young. Let the mother go, but you may take the young. This will ensure your well-being and prolong your life.

When you make a vow to the LORD your God, do not delay in fulfilling it. The LORD your God will demand it from you, and you will be guilty of sin. If you refrain from making a vow, you will not be guilty. Whatever your lips utter, you must be sure to do, because you made your vow freely to the LORD your God with your own mouth.

Do not deny justice to a foreigner or an orphan, and do not take a widow's cloak as a pledge. Remember that you were slaves in Egypt, and the LORD your God redeemed you from there. That is why I command you to do this.

When you build a new house, make a parapet around your roof to prevent anyone from falling off and bringing bloodshed on your house.

Do not plant two kinds of seed in your vineyard; if you do, not only the crops you plant but also the fruit of the vineyard will be defiled.

When you enter your neighbor's vineyard, you may eat all the grapes you want, but do not put any in your basket. When you enter your neighbor's grainfield, you may pick kernels with your hands, but do not put a sickle to their standing grain.

When you harvest your field and overlook a sheaf, do not go back to get it. Leave it for the foreigner, the fatherless, and the widow, so that the LORD your God may bless you in all the work of your hands.

Do not plow with an ox and a donkey yoked together. Do not wear clothes of wool and linen woven together. Make tassels on the four corners of the cloak you wear.

When you beat the olives from your trees, do not go over the branches a second time. Leave what remains for the foreigner, the fatherless, and the widow. When you harvest the grapes in your vineyard, do not go over the vines again. Leave what remains for the foreigner, the fatherless, and the widow. Remember that you were slaves in Egypt. That is why I command you to do this.

If people have a dispute, they are to take it to court, and the judges will decide the case, acquitting the innocent and condemning the guilty. If the guilty person deserves to be beaten, the judge shall make them lie down and have them flogged in his presence with the number of lashes the crime deserves, but no more than forty. If the guilty person is flogged more than that, your fellow Israelite will be degraded in your eyes.

Do not muzzle an ox while it is treading out the grain.

If brothers are living together and one of them dies without a son, his widow must not marry outside the family. Her husband's brother shall take her and marry her and fulfill the duty of a brother-in-law to her. The first son she bears shall carry on the name of the dead brother so that his name will not be blotted out from Israel. If the man does not want to marry his brother's widow, she shall go to the elders at the town gate and say, "My husband's brother refuses to carry on his brother's name in Israel. He will not fulfill the duty of a brother-in-law to me." Then the elders of his town shall summon him and talk to him. If he persists in saying, "I do not want to marry her," his brother's widow shall go up to him in the presence of the elders, take off one of his sandals, spit in his face, and say, "This is what is done to the man who will not build up his brother's family line." That man's line shall be known in Israel as The Family of the Unsandaled.

Remember what the Amalekites did to you along the way when you came out of Egypt. When you were weary and worn out, they met you on your journey and attacked all who were lagging behind; they had no fear of God. When the LORD your God gives you rest from all the enemies around you in the land He is giving you to possess as an inheritance, you shall blot out the name of Amalek from under heaven. Do not forget!

If two men are fighting and the wife of one of them comes to rescue her husband from his assailant, and she reaches out and seizes him by his private parts, you shall cut off her hand. Show her no pity.

When you have entered the land the LORD your God is giving you as an inheritance and have taken possession of it and settled in it, take some of the firstfruits of all that you produce from the soil of the land the LORD your God is giving you and put them in a basket.When you bring the first fruits from your land, which the LORD your God has given you, place them in a basket and go to the place the LORD chooses for His name to dwell. Approach the priest in office at that time and say, "I declare today to the LORD your God that I have come to the land the LORD swore to our ancestors to give us." The priest will take the basket from your hand and set it down in front of the altar of the LORD your God. Then you shall declare before the LORD your God: "My ancestor was a wandering Aramean who went down to Egypt and lived there, few in number, but became a great, powerful, and populous nation. The Egyptians mistreated us, oppressed us, and subjected us to harsh labor. We cried out to the LORD, the God of our ancestors, and He heard our voice, saw our misery, toil, and oppression. The LORD brought us out of Egypt with a mighty hand and an outstretched arm, with great terror, signs, and wonders. He brought us to this place and gave us this land, a land flowing with milk and honey. Now I bring the first fruits of the soil that you, LORD, have given me." Place the basket before the LORD your God and bow down before Him. Rejoice in all the good things the LORD your God has given to you and your household, along with the Levites and the foreigners residing among you.

Do not use dishonest weights and measures. Use accurate and honest weights and measures, so that you may live long in the land the LORD your God is giving you. For the LORD detests anyone who does these things, anyone who deals dishonestly.

When you have finished setting aside a tenth of all your produce in the third year, the year of the tithe, and have given it to the Levite, the foreigner, the fatherless, and the widow, so that they may eat in your towns and be satisfied, declare before the LORD your God: "I have removed from my house the sacred portion and have given it to the Levite, the foreigner, the fatherless, and the widow, according to all you commanded. I have not turned aside from your commands nor have I forgotten any of them. I have not eaten any of the sacred portion while in mourning, nor have I removed any of it while I was unclean, nor have I offered any of it to the dead. I have obeyed the LORD my God; I have done everything you commanded me. Look down from heaven, your holy dwelling place, and bless your people Israel and the land you have given us as you promised on oath to our ancestors, a land flowing with milk and honey."

The LORD your God commands you this day to follow these decrees and laws; carefully observe them with all your heart and with all your soul. Moses and the elders of Israel commanded the people: "Keep all these commands that I give you today. When you have crossed the Jordan into the land the LORD your God is giving you, set up some large stones and coat them with plaster. Write on them all the words of this law when you have crossed over to enter the land the LORD your God is giving you, a land flowing with milk and honey, just as the LORD, the God of your ancestors, promised you."

Moses and the priests, who are Levites, said to all Israel: "Be silent, Israel, and listen! You have now become the people of the LORD your God. Obey the LORD your God and follow His commands and decrees that I give you today."

Moses commanded the people on the same day: "When you have crossed the Jordan, these tribes shall stand on Mount Gerizim to bless the people: Simeon, Levi, Judah, Issachar, Joseph, and Benjamin. And these tribes shall stand on Mount Ebal to pronounce curses: Reuben, Gad, Asher, Zebulun, Dan, and Naphtali. The Levites shall recite to all the people of Israel in a loud voice:

'Cursed is anyone who makes an idol—a thing detestable to the LORD, the work of skilled hands—and sets it up in secret.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who dishonors their father or mother.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who moves their neighbor's boundary stone.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who leads the blind astray on the road.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who withholds justice from the foreigner, the fatherless, or the widow.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who sleeps with his father's wife, for he dishonors his father's bed.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who has sexual relations with any animal.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who sleeps with his sister, the daughter of his father or the daughter of his mother.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who sleeps with his mother-in-law.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who kills their neighbor secretly.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who accepts a bribe to kill an innocent person.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

'Cursed is anyone who does not uphold the words of this law by carrying them out.' Then all the people shall say, 'Amen!'

If you fully obey the LORD your God and carefully follow all His commands I give you today, the LORD your God will set you high above all the nations on earth. All these blessings will come on you and accompany you if you obey the LORD your God:

You will be blessed in the city and blessed in the country. The fruit of your womb will be blessed, and the crops of your land and the young of your livestock—the calves of your herds and the lambs of your flocks. Your basket and your kneading trough will be blessed. You will be blessed when you come in and blessed when you go out.

The LORD will grant that the enemies who rise up against you will be defeated before you. They will come at you from one direction but flee from you in seven. The LORD will send a blessing on your barns and on everything you put your hand to. The LORD your God will bless you in the land He is giving you. The LORD will establish you as His holy people, as He promised you on oath, if you keep the commands of the LORD your God and walk in obedience to Him. Then all the peoples on earth will see that you are called by the name of the LORD, and they will fear you. The LORD will grant you abundant prosperity—in the fruit of your womb, the young of your livestock, and the crops of your ground—in the land He swore to your ancestors to give you. The LORD will open the heavens, the storehouse of His bounty, to send rain on your land in season and to bless all the work of your hands. You will lend to many nations but will borrow from none. The LORD will make you the head, not the tail. If you pay attention to the commands of the LORD your God that I give you this day and carefully follow them, you will always be at the top, never at the bottom. Do not turn aside from any of the commands I give you today, to the right or to the left, following other gods and serving them.

However, if you do not obey the LORD your God and do not carefully follow all His commands and decrees I am giving you today, all these curses will come on you and overtake you:

The LORD will afflict you with the boils of Egypt and with tumors, festering sores, and the itch, from which you cannot be cured.The LORD will strike you with painful boils, scabs, and itching that cannot be healed. You will plant many seeds in your fields but harvest little because locusts will consume your crops. You will be cursed in the city and in the countryside. Your basket and kneading trough will be cursed. The offspring of your body, the produce of your land, and the young of your livestock will be cursed. You will be cursed when you come in and when you go out.

The LORD will strike you with madness, blindness, and confusion. You will grope around at noon as a blind person gropes in the dark. You will not succeed in anything you do; you will be oppressed and robbed continually, with no one to save you. You will plant vineyards and tend them but will not drink the wine or gather the grapes because worms will eat them.

The LORD will send curses, confusion, and rebuke in everything you do until you are destroyed and perish quickly because of the evil you have done in forsaking Him. You will be engaged to a woman, but another man will sleep with her. You will build a house but not live in it. You will plant a vineyard but not enjoy its fruit. Your ox will be slaughtered before your eyes, but you will not eat any of it. Your donkey will be forcibly taken from you and not returned. Your sheep will be given to your enemies, and no one will rescue them.

You will have olive trees throughout your land but will not use the oil because the olives will drop off. The LORD will afflict you with diseases until you are wiped out from the land you are entering to possess. Your sons and daughters will be given to another nation, and you will long for them all day but be powerless to help. You will have children, but they will be taken into captivity.

The LORD will strike you with wasting disease, fever, inflammation, scorching heat, drought, blight, and mildew, which will plague you until you perish. The sky over your head will be bronze, and the ground beneath you iron. A nation you do not know will eat the fruit of your land and labor, and you will be oppressed and crushed continually. You will be driven mad by what you see.

All your trees and the fruit of your land will be devoured by locusts. The LORD will turn the rain of your land into dust and powder; it will come down from the skies until you are destroyed. The LORD will strike you with painful boils from the soles of your feet to the top of your head. The foreigner living among you will rise higher and higher, while you sink lower and lower. They will lend to you, but you will not lend to them. They will be the head, and you will be the tail.

The LORD will bring a nation from far away, from the ends of the earth, like an eagle swooping down, a nation whose language you do not understand, a fierce nation that shows no respect for the old or favor to the young. They will devour the young of your livestock and the crops of your land until you are destroyed. They will besiege all the cities throughout your land until your high fortified walls fall.

You will eat the flesh of your own sons and daughters during the siege and distress your enemies will impose on you. The most gentle and sensitive man among you will begrudge his brother, the wife he loves, and the rest of his children, not giving them any of the flesh of his children that he is eating. The most gentle and sensitive woman among you will begrudge the husband she loves, her son, and her daughter, not sharing with them the afterbirth from her womb or the children she bears.

If you do not carefully follow all the words of this law, the LORD will bring upon you extraordinary plagues and severe illnesses. He will bring back upon you all the diseases of Egypt, which you dreaded, and they will cling to you. Every sickness and plague not recorded in this book of the law will the LORD bring upon you until you are destroyed. You will be left few in number, whereas you were as numerous as the stars in the sky, because you did not obey the LORD your God.

Just as the LORD took delight in making you prosper and increase in number, so He will take delight in ruining and destroying you. You will be uprooted from the land you are entering to possess. The LORD will scatter you among all nations, from one end of the earth to the other. There you will worship other gods, gods of wood and stone, which neither you nor your ancestors have known. Among those nations, you will find no repose, no resting place for the sole of your foot. The LORD will give you an anxious mind, eyes weary with longing, and a despairing heart. You will live in constant suspense, filled with dread both night and day, never sure of your life. In the morning, you will say, "If only it were evening!" and in the evening, "If only it were morning!" because of the terror that will fill your hearts and the sights you will see.

The LORD will send you back in ships to Egypt on a journey I said you should never make again. There you will offer yourselves for sale to your enemies as male and female slaves, but no one will buy you.

These are the terms of the covenant the LORD commanded Moses to make with the Israelites in Moab, in addition to the covenant He had made with them at Horeb.Moses addressed all of Israel, reminding them of the great trials and wonders they witnessed in Egypt. Despite these signs, the LORD had not yet given them the understanding to fully grasp His works. For forty years, He led them through the wilderness, ensuring their clothes and shoes did not wear out, and provided for them so they would recognize Him as their God.

Moses warned against turning away from the LORD to serve other gods, as this would bring severe consequences. He recounted how they defeated Sihon, king of Heshbon, and Og, king of Bashan, and took their land as an inheritance. He urged them to observe the covenant's words to prosper in all they do.

If anyone hears the words of the curse and thinks they will have peace despite their stubbornness, the LORD's anger will be kindled against them, and all the curses written in the book will fall upon them. Future generations and foreigners will see the land's devastation and ask why the LORD has done this. The answer will be because the people forsook the covenant and worshipped other gods.

However, if they return to the LORD with all their heart and soul, He will have compassion and gather them from all nations. He will bring them back to the land their ancestors possessed and bless them abundantly. The LORD will put curses on their enemies and make them prosperous if they obey His commandments.

Moses emphasized that the commandment is not too difficult or distant; it is within their reach to follow. He set before them life and good, death and evil, urging them to choose life by loving the LORD and keeping His commandments. This choice would ensure their prosperity and longevity in the land promised to their ancestors.

Moses, now 120 years old, informed the people that he could no longer lead them, and the LORD had appointed Joshua to take them into the promised land. He encouraged Joshua to be strong and courageous, assuring him that the LORD would be with him.

Moses wrote down the law and instructed it to be read every seven years during the Feast of Tabernacles so that all Israel, including children and foreigners, would learn to fear the LORD and follow His commandments. The LORD then called Moses and Joshua to the tent of meeting, where He appeared in a pillar of cloud and prepared to give Joshua his charge.Moses warned the Israelites that if they turned to foreign gods and broke the covenant, God's anger would be kindled against them. He would hide His face, and they would face many troubles, realizing that these evils came because God was not among them. Moses finished writing the law and instructed the Levites to place it beside the Ark of the Covenant as a witness against the people, knowing their rebellious nature.

Moses then commanded the Israelites to write and teach a song to their children as a witness against them when they turned to other gods after entering the promised land. He charged Joshua to be strong and courageous, assuring him that God would be with him.

Moses gathered all the elders and officers to speak these words, calling heaven and earth as witnesses. He knew that after his death, the people would become corrupt and face evil days because of their actions. Moses then recited the song to the assembly, emphasizing God's greatness, faithfulness, and justice.

He reminded them of God's care and provision, contrasting it with their unfaithfulness and idolatry. God would hide His face and bring calamities upon them for their disobedience. However, He would also judge His people and have compassion when they were left with no help.

Moses urged the people to set their hearts on his words and teach them to their children, as these words were their life and would prolong their days in the promised land. God then instructed Moses to go up Mount Nebo to see the land of Canaan, which he would not enter, and to die there, as Aaron did, because of their disobedience at the waters of Meribath-kadesh.Moses, the man of God, blessed the Israelites before his death. He said, "The LORD came from Sinai, shone from Seir, and appeared from Mount Paran with a fiery law in His right hand. He loves His people, and all His holy ones are in His care. They sit at His feet and receive His words. Moses gave us the law, an inheritance for the congregation of Jacob. There was a king in Jeshurun when the leaders of the people and the tribes of Israel gathered together.

"Let Reuben live and not die, even though his men are few. For Levi, he said, 'Your Thummim and Urim belong to your faithful one, whom you tested at Massah and contended with at the waters of Meribah. He said of his father and mother, "I do not regard them"; he did not acknowledge his brothers or his children, for they kept Your word and guarded Your covenant. They will teach Jacob Your laws and Israel Your instructions. They will offer incense before You and whole burnt offerings on Your altar. Bless his substance, LORD, and accept the work of his hands. Strike down those who rise against him and hate him, so they do not rise again.'

"For Judah, he said, 'Hear, LORD, the voice of Judah and bring him to his people. His hands will defend him, and You will be a help against his enemies.' For Benjamin, he said, 'The beloved of the LORD will dwell in safety by Him. He covers him all day long and dwells between his shoulders.'

"For Joseph, he said, 'Blessed by the LORD is his land, with the precious things of heaven, the dew, and the deep waters beneath. Blessed with the precious fruits of the sun, the rich yield of the moons, the best of the ancient mountains, and the precious things of the everlasting hills. Blessed with the precious things of the earth and its fullness, and the favor of Him who dwelt in the burning bush. Let these blessings come upon the head of Joseph, the prince among his brothers. His majesty is like a firstborn bull, and his horns are like the horns of a wild ox. With them, he will gore the peoples to the ends of the earth. These are the ten thousands of Ephraim and the thousands of Manasseh.'

"For Zebulun, he said, 'Rejoice, Zebulun, in your going out, and Issachar, in your tents. They will call peoples to the mountain, where they will offer righteous sacrifices. They will draw from the abundance of the seas and the hidden treasures of the sand.'

"For Gad, he said, 'Blessed is He who enlarges Gad. He lives like a lioness and tears at the arm and the crown of the head. He chose the best land for himself, where the leader's portion was reserved. He came with the heads of the people and executed the LORD's justice and His ordinances with Israel.'

"For Dan, he said, 'Dan is a lion's cub, leaping out from Bashan.' For Naphtali, he said, 'Naphtali is satisfied with favor and full of the LORD's blessing. Possess the west and the south.' For Asher, he said, 'Asher is blessed above sons. Let him be favored by his brothers and dip his foot in oil. Your bars will be iron and bronze, and your strength will last as long as your days.'

"There is no one like God, O Jeshurun, who rides the heavens to help you and in His majesty on the skies. The eternal God is your refuge, and underneath are the everlasting arms. He will drive out your enemy before you and command, 'Destroy!' Israel will live in safety, Jacob's spring secure in a land of grain and new wine, where the heavens drop dew. Blessed are you, Israel! Who is like you, a people saved by the LORD? He is your shield and helper, your glorious sword. Your enemies will cower before you, and you will tread on their heights."

Moses then went up from the plains of Moab to Mount Nebo, to the top of Pisgah, across from Jericho. The LORD showed him all the land, from Gilead to Dan, all of Naphtali, the land of Ephraim and Manasseh, all the land of Judah as far as the Mediterranean Sea, the Negev, and the whole region from the Valley of Jericho, the City of Palms, to Zoar. The LORD said to him, "This is the land I promised to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, saying, 'I will give it to your descendants.' I have let you see it with your eyes, but you will not cross over into it."

So Moses, the servant of the LORD, died there in Moab, as the LORD had said. He was buried in Moab, in the valley opposite Beth Peor, but to this day no one knows where his grave is. Moses was 120 years old when he died, yet his eyes were not weak nor his strength gone. The Israelites grieved for Moses in the plains of Moab for thirty days, until the time of weeping and mourning was over.

Joshua son of Nun was filled with the spirit of wisdom because Moses had laid his hands on him. The Israelites listened to him and did what the LORD had commanded Moses. Since then, no prophet has risen in Israel like Moses, whom the LORD knew face to face. He did all the signs and wonders the LORD sent him to do in Egypt—to Pharaoh, to all his officials, and to his whole land. For no one has ever shown the mighty power or performed the awesome deeds that Moses did in the sight of all Israel.
